وَهَذَا الْقَوْلُ هُوَ الْأَشْهَرُ وَالْأَلْيَقُ وَالْأَنْسَبُ بِسِيَاقِ الْقِصَّةِ وَمَعَانِي الْكَلَامِ. وَقَدْ حَكَاهُ الْمَاوَرْدِيُّ فِي تَفْسِيرِهِ، وَانْتَدَبَ لِنَصْرِهِ الْإِمَامُ الْعَلَّامَةُ أَبُو الْعَبَّاسِ ابْنُ تَيميَّة، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، فَأَفْرَدَهُ بِتَصْنِيفٍ عَلَى حِدَةٍ 

وَقَدْ قِيلَ: إِنَّ ذَلِكَ مِنْ كَلَامِ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، مِنْ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿ذَلِكَ لِيَعْلَمَ أَنِّي لَمْ أَخُنْهُ﴾ فِي زَوْجَتِهِ ﴿بِالْغَيْبِ﴾ الْآيَتَيْنِ أَيْ: إِنَّمَا رَدَدْتُ الرَّسُولَ لِيَعْلَمَ الْمَلِكُ بَرَاءَتِي وَلِيَعْلَمَ الْعَزِيزُ ﴿أَنِّي لَمْ أَخُنْهُ﴾ فِي زَوْجَتِهِ ﴿بِالْغَيْبِ﴾ ﴿وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَهْدِي كَيْدَ الْخَائِنِينَ وَمَا أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِي إِنَّ النَّفْسَ لأمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ﴾ [الْآيَةَ] وَهَذَا الْقَوْلُ هُوَ الَّذِي لَمَّ يَحْكِ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ وَلَا ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ سِوَاهُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو كُرَيْب، حَدَّثَنَا وَكِيع، عَنْ إِسْرَائِيلُ، عَنْ سِمَاك، عَنْ عِكْرِمة، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: لَمَّا جَمَعَ الْمَلِكُ النِّسْوَةَ فَسَأَلَهُنَّ: هَلْ رَاوَدْتُنَّ يُوسُفَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ؟ ﴿قُلْنَ حَاشَ لِلَّهِ مَا عَلِمْنَا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ سُوءٍ قَالَتِ امْرَأَةُ الْعَزِيزِ الآنَ حَصْحَصَ الْحَقُّ أَنَا رَاوَدْتُهُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَإِنَّهُ لَمِنَ الصَّادِقِينَ﴾ قَالَ يُوسُفُ ﴿ذَلِكَ لِيَعْلَمَ أَنِّي لَمْ أَخُنْهُ بِالْغَيْبِ [وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَهْدِي كَيْدَ الْخَائِنِينَ] ﴾ قَالَ: فَقَالَ لَهُ جِبْرِيلُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: وَلَا يَوْمَ هَمَمْتَ بِمَا هَمَمْتَ بِهِ. فَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَا أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِي إِنَّ النَّفْسَ لأمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ﴾ 

وَهَكَذَا قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْر، وَعِكْرِمَةُ، وَابْنُ أَبِي الهُذَيل، وَالضَّحَّاكُ، وَالْحَسَنُ، وَقَتَادَةُ، والسُّدي. وَالْقَوْلُ الْأَوَّلُ أَقْوَى وَأُظْهِرُ؛ لِأَنَّ سِيَاقَ الْكَلَامِ كُلِّهِ مِنْ كَلَامِ امْرَأَةِ الْعَزِيزِ بِحَضْرَةِ الْمَلِكِ، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ يُوسُفُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، عِنْدَهُمْ، بَلْ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ أَحْضَرَهُ الْمَلِكُ.

---

## 12:54-55 — verses 54-55 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Most High says, informing about the king when the innocence of Yusuf (peace be upon him) and the purity of his honor from what had been attributed to him became established, He said: {Bring him to me, that I may take him exclusively for myself} meaning: I will make him one of my inner circle and my counselors. {And when he spoke with him} meaning: the king addressed him and came to know him, and saw his excellence and his outstanding merit, and learned what character, disposition, and perfection he possessed, the king said to him: {Indeed, you are today, with us, established in position and trusted} meaning: you have proven to be, in our estimation, one of standing and trustworthiness. So Yusuf (peace be upon him) said: {Place me in charge of the storehouses of the land; indeed, I am a guardian, knowledgeable} He praised himself, and this is permissible for a man when his true character is unknown, out of necessity. He mentioned that he was {a guardian} meaning: a trustworthy custodian, {knowledgeable} possessing knowledge and insight into what he would be entrusted with.

Shaybah ibn Na'amah said: "a guardian over what is entrusted to me, knowledgeable about the years of drought." Reported by Ibn Abi Hatim.

He asked for the position because he knew his own capability for it, and because of the benefits it held for the people. He asked specifically to be placed in charge of the storehouses of the land, which were the granaries in which the harvests were gathered, in preparation for the years he had informed them about, so that he could manage matters for them in the most cautious, most beneficial, and most prudent manner. He was granted this out of eagerness for him and as an honor to him. It is for this reason that the Most High says:

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى إِخْبَارًا عَنِ الْمَلِكِ حِينَ تَحَقَقَ بَرَاءَةَ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَنَزَاهَةَ عرْضه مِمَّا نُسِبَ إِلَيْهِ، قَالَ: ﴿ائْتُونِي بِهِ أَسْتَخْلِصْهُ لِنَفْسِي﴾ أَيْ: أَجْعَلُهُ مِنْ خَاصَّتِي وَأَهْلِ مَشُورَتِي ﴿فَلَمَّا كَلَّمَهُ﴾ أَيْ: خَاطَبَهُ الْمَلِكُ وَعَرَفَهُ، وَرَأَى فَضْلَهُ وَبَرَاعَتَهُ، وَعَلِمَ مَا هُوَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ خَلْق وخُلُق وَكَمَالٍ قَالَ لَهُ الْمَلِكُ: ﴿إِنَّكَ الْيَوْمَ لَدَيْنَا مَكِينٌ أَمِينٌ﴾ أَيْ: إِنَّكَ عِنْدَنَا قَدْ بَقِيتَ ذَا مَكَانَةٍ وَأَمَانَةٍ، فَقَالَ يُوسُفُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: ﴿اجْعَلْنِي عَلَى خَزَائِنِ الأرْضِ إِنِّي حَفِيظٌ عَلِيمٌ﴾ مَدَحَ نَفْسَهُ، وَيَجُوزُ لِلرَّجُلِ ذَلِكَ إِذَا جُهِل أَمْرُهُ، لِلْحَاجَةِ. وَذَكَرَ أَنَّهُ ﴿حَفِيظٌ﴾ أَيْ: خَازِنٌ أَمِينٌ، ﴿عَلِيمٌ﴾ ذُو عِلْمٍ وبصرَ بِمَا يَتَوَلَّاهُ .

قَالَ شَيْبَةُ بْنُ نَعَامَةَ: حَفِيظٌ لِمَا اسْتَوْدَعَتْنِي، عَلِيمٌ بِسِني الجَدْب. رَوَاهُ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ.

وَسَأَلَ الْعَمَلَ لِعِلْمِهِ بِقُدْرَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ، وَلِمَا فِي ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْمَصَالِحِ لِلنَّاسِ وَإِنَّمَا سَأَلَ أَنْ يُجْعَل عَلَى خَزَائِنِ الْأَرْضِ، وَهِيَ الْأَهْرَامُ الَّتِي يُجْمَعُ فِيهَا الْغَلَّاتُ، لِمَا يَسْتَقْبِلُونَهُ مِنَ السِّنِينَ الَّتِي أَخْبَرَهُمْ بِشَأْنِهَا، لِيَتَصَرَّفَ لَهُمْ عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الْأَحْوَطِ وَالْأَصْلَحِ وَالْأَرْشَدِ، فَأُجِيبَ إِلَى ذَلِكَ رَغْبَةً فِيهِ، وتكرِمَةً لَهُ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ تَعَالَى:

---

## 12:56-57 — verses 56-57 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says: {And thus We established Yusuf in the land}, meaning the land of Egypt, {settling wherever he wished}.

Al-Suddi and Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: he could act as he wished within it.

Ibn Jarir said: he could take up dwelling wherever he wished after the hardship, the imprisonment, and the captivity. {We grant Our mercy to whom We will, and We do not let the reward of those who do good be lost}, meaning: We did not let Yusuf's patience in the face of his brothers' harm, and his patience under imprisonment because of the wife of al-Aziz, go to waste. For this reason, God, mighty and exalted, gave him in consequence safety, victory, and support. {And We do not let the reward of those who do good be lost. And the reward of the Hereafter is better for those who believe and were mindful of God}. The Almighty informs that what God stored up for His prophet Yusuf, peace be upon him, in the abode of the Hereafter is greater, more abundant, and more majestic than what He granted him of authority and power in this world, just as He said regarding Sulayman, peace be upon him: {This is Our gift, so give freely or withhold, without any reckoning. And indeed for him with Us is nearness and a good place of return} [Sad: 39, 40].

The point is that Yusuf, peace be upon him, was appointed by the king of Egypt, al-Rayyan ibn al-Walid, to the position of vizier in the lands of Egypt, taking the place of the one who had bought him in Egypt, the husband of the woman who had tried to seduce him. And the king embraced Islam at the hands of Yusuf, peace be upon him.

This was stated by Mujahid. Muhammad ibn Ishaq said: when Yusuf said to the king, {Place me over the storehouses of the land, for I am trustworthy and knowledgeable}, the king said: I have done so. So he appointed him, as they have mentioned, to the position of Itfir, and removed Itfir from the post he had held. God, mighty and exalted, says: {And thus We established Yusuf in the land, settling wherever he wished. We grant Our mercy to whom We will, and We do not let the reward of those who do good be lost}. It was mentioned to me, and God knows best, that Itfir died during those nights, and that the king al-Rayyan ibn al-Walid married Yusuf to Itfir's wife, Ra'il. And it is said that when she entered upon him he said: Is this not better than what you used to desire? They claim she said: O truthful one, do not blame me, for I was a woman as you see, beautiful and comely, living in comfort amid kingship and worldly ease, while my husband did not approach women, and you were as God made you in your beauty and form, as you have seen. They claim he found her still a virgin, and that he then had relations with her, and she bore him two sons, Ifra'im ibn Yusuf and Misha ibn Yusuf. To Ifra'im was born Nun, the father of Yusha ibn Nun, and of Rahmah, the wife of Ayyub, peace be upon him.

Al-Fudayl ibn Iyad said: the wife of al-Aziz stood on the side of the road until Yusuf passed by, and she said: Praise be to God, who makes slaves kings through obedience to Him, and makes kings slaves through disobedience to Him.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ مَكَّنَّا لِيُوسُفَ فِي الأرْضِ﴾ أَيْ: أَرْضِ مِصْرَ، ﴿يَتَبَوَّأُ مِنْهَا حَيْثُ يَشَاءُ﴾

قَالَ السُّدِّي، وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: يَتَصَرَّفُ فِيهَا كَيْفَ يَشَاءُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: يَتَّخِذُ مِنْهَا مَنْزِلًا حَيْثُ يَشَاءُ بَعْدَ الضِّيقِ وَالْحَبْسِ وَالْإِسَارِ. ﴿نُصِيبُ بِرَحْمَتِنَا مَنْ نَشَاءُ وَلا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ﴾ أَيْ: وَمَا أَضَعْنَا صَبْرَ يُوسُفَ عَلَى أَذَى إِخْوَتِهِ، وَصَبْرَهُ عَلَى الْحَبْسِ بِسَبَبِ امْرَأَةِ الْعَزِيزِ؛ فَلِهَذَا أَعْقَبَهُ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ السَّلَامَةَ وَالنَّصْرَ وَالتَّأْيِيدَ، ﴿وَلا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ وَلأجْرُ الآخِرَةِ خَيْرٌ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَكَانُوا يَتَّقُونَ﴾ يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى أَنَّ مَا ادَّخَرَهُ اللَّهُ لِنَبِيِّهِ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، فِي الدَّارِ الْآخِرَةِ أَعْظَمُ وَأَكْثَرُ وَأَجَلُّ، مِمَّا خَوَّلَهُ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ وَالنُّفُوذِ فِي الدُّنْيَا كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي حَقِّ سُلَيْمَانَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: ﴿هَذَا عَطَاؤُنَا فَامْنُنْ أَوْ أَمْسِكْ بِغَيْرِ حِسَابٍ وَإِنَّ لَهُ عِنْدَنَا لَزُلْفَى وَحُسْنَ مَآبٍ﴾ [ص: ٣٩، ٤٠] .

وَالْغَرَضُ أَنَّ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَلَّاهُ مَلك مِصْرَ الريانُ بْنُ الْوَلِيدِ الْوَزَارَةَ فِي بِلَادِ مِصْرَ، مَكَانَ الَّذِي اشْتَرَاهُ مِنْ مِصْرَ زَوْجِ الَّتِي رَاوَدَتْهُ، وَأَسْلَمَ الْمَلِكُ عَلَى يَدَيْ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ.

قَالَهُ مُجَاهِدٌ. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ لَمَّا قَالَ يُوسُفُ لِلْمَلِكِ: ﴿اجْعَلْنِي عَلَى خَزَائِنِ الأرْضِ إِنِّي حَفِيظٌ عَلِيمٌ﴾ قَالَ الْمَلِكُ: قَدْ فَعَلْتُ. فَوَلَّاهُ فِيمَا ذَكَرُوا عَمَلَ إِطْفِيرَ وَعَزَلَ إِطْفِيرَ عَمَّا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ، يَقُولُ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ مَكَّنَّا لِيُوسُفَ فِي الأرْضِ يَتَبَوَّأُ مِنْهَا حَيْثُ يَشَاءُ نُصِيبُ بِرَحْمَتِنَا مَنْ نَشَاءُ وَلا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ﴾ فَذُكِرَ لِي -وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ -أَنَّ إِطْفِيرَ هَلك فِي تِلْكَ اللَّيَالِي، وَأَنَّ الْمَلِكَ الرَّيَّانَ بْنَ الْوَلِيدِ زوَّج يُوسُفَ امْرَأَةَ إِطْفِيرَ رَاعِيلَ، وَأَنَّهَا حِينَ دَخَلَتْ عَلَيْهِ قَالَ: أَلَيْسَ هَذَا خَيْرًا مِمَّا كُنْتِ تُرِيدِينَ؟ قَالَ: فَيَزْعُمُونَ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: أَيُّهَا الصِّدِّيقُ، لَا تَلُمْنِي، فَإِنِّي كُنْتُ امْرَأَةً كَمَا تَرَى حَسْنَاءَ جَمِيلَةً، نَاعِمَةً فِي مُلْكٍ وَدُنْيَا، وَكَانَ صَاحِبِي لَا يَأْتِي النِّسَاءَ، وَكُنْتَ كَمَا جَعَلَكَ اللَّهُ فِي حُسْنِكَ وَهَيْئَتِكَ عَلَى مَا رَأَيْتَ، فَيَزْعُمُونَ أَنَّهُ وَجَدَهَا عَذْرَاءَ، فَأَصَابَهَا فَوَلَدَتْ لَهُ رَجُلَيْنِ أَفْرَائِيمَ بن يوسف، وميشا بن يُوسُفَ وَوُلِدَ لِأَفْرَائِيمَ نُونٌ، وَالِدُ يُوشَعَ بْنِ نُونٍ، وَرَحْمَةَ امْرَأَةِ أَيُّوبَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ.

وَقَالَ الْفُضَيْلُ بْنُ عِيَاضٍ: وَقَفَتِ امْرَأَةُ الْعَزِيزِ عَلَى ظَهْرِ الطَّرِيقِ، حَتَّى مَرّ يُوسُفُ، فَقَالَتْ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي جَعَلَ الْعَبِيدَ مُلُوكًا بِطَاعَتِهِ، وَالْمُلُوكَ عَبِيدًا بِمَعْصِيَتِهِ.

---

## 12:58-62 — verses 58-62 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Al-Suddi, Muhammad ibn Ishaq, and other commentators mentioned that the reason that brought the brothers of Yusuf to the land of Egypt was that Yusuf, peace be upon him, when he took up the office of vizier in Egypt, and the seven fruitful years passed, followed by the years of drought, and the famine encompassed the land of Egypt in its entirety, and reached the land of Canaan, which was where Ya'qub, peace be upon him, and his sons were. At that time Yusuf, peace be upon him, took great care of the people's crops, gathering them in the best manner, so that an immense quantity resulted from that, and numerous vast granaries. People came to him from every region and every district to obtain provisions for themselves and their families, and no man was given more than one camel-load per year. Yusuf, peace be upon him, would not satisfy his own hunger, nor did he, the king, and their soldiers eat except one meal in the middle of the day, so that the people might be sufficiently provided for from what was in their hands throughout the seven years. This was a mercy from Allah upon the people of Egypt.

As for what some commentators have mentioned, that he sold to them in the first year in exchange for wealth, in the second year in exchange for goods, in the third for such and such, and in the fourth for such and such, until he had bought them with their own persons and their children after having taken possession of everything they owned, then afterward freed them and returned all their wealth to them, Allah knows best regarding the truth of this. It is among the Isra'iliyyat (reports of Israelite origin) which are neither confirmed nor denied.

The point is that among the group who came for provisions were the brothers of Yusuf, at their father's command to them regarding that. For it had reached them that the 'Aziz of Egypt was giving people food in exchange for its price, so they took with them goods to exchange for food, and ten men set out riding, while Ya'qub, peace be upon him, kept back with him Binyamin, the full brother of Yusuf, peace be upon them both, who was the most beloved of his children to him after Yusuf. When they entered upon Yusuf, and he was sitting in his majesty, authority, and eminence, he recognized them the moment he looked at them, {while they did not recognize him}, meaning they did not know him, because they had parted from him when he was a small child, and they had sold him to travelers, not knowing where he would be taken, nor did they ever imagine in themselves that he would come to be what he had become. For this reason they did not recognize him, whereas he recognized them.

Al-Suddi and others mentioned that he began to address them, saying to them as one reproaching them: "What has brought you to my land?" They said: "O 'Aziz, we have come for provisions." He said: "Perhaps you are spies?" They said: "God forbid." He said: "Then where are you from?" They said: "From the land of Canaan, and our father is Ya'qub, the Prophet of Allah." He said: "Does he have children besides you?" They said: "Yes, we were twelve, but the youngest of us went away and perished in the wilderness, and he was the most beloved of us to our father. His full brother remains, and our father has kept him back so as to console himself with him for the one he lost." So he ordered that they be lodged and honored.

{And when he had furnished them with their provisions}, meaning he gave them their measure in full and loaded their goods for them, he said: "Bring me this brother of yours whom you have mentioned, so that I may know the truth of what you have said." {Do you not see that I give full measure and that I am the best of hosts?} He was encouraging them to return to him. Then he warned them, saying: {But if you do not bring him to me, there shall be no measure for you with me, nor shall you come near me}, meaning if you do not bring him with you the second time, then there will be no provisions for you with me. {Nor shall you come near me. They said: We will endeavor to persuade his father to part with him, and we will surely do so}, meaning we will strive by every possible means to bring him to you, and we will spare no effort, so that you may know the truth of what we have said.

Al-Suddi mentioned that he took hostages from them until they should bring him along with them. There is something questionable in this, because he had treated them well and encouraged them greatly, and this was due to his eagerness for their return.

{And he said to his young men}, meaning his servants, {Put their merchandise}, which is what they had brought with them to exchange for provisions, {into their saddlebags}, meaning into their belongings, without their noticing, {so that they may return} with it.

It has been said that Yusuf, peace be upon him, feared that they might not have other goods with which to return for provisions. It has also been said that he felt reluctant to take from his father and brothers a price in exchange for the food. And it has been said that he wanted them to return it, upon finding it in their belongings, out of scrupulousness and piety, since he knew that this was their way. And Allah knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

ذَكَرَ السُّدي، وَمُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ، وَغَيْرُهُمَا مِنَ الْمُفَسِّرِينَ: أَنَّ السَّبَبَ الَّذِي أَقْدَمَ إِخْوَةَ يُوسُفَ بِلَادَ مِصْرَ، أَنَّ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، لَمَّا بَاشَرَ الْوَزَارَةَ بِمِصْرَ، وَمَضَتِ السَّبْعُ السِّنِينَ الْمُخْصِبَةُ، ثُمَّ تَلَتْهَا سنينُ الْجَدْبِ، وَعَمَّ الْقَحْطُ بِلَادَ مِصْرَ بِكَمَالِهَا، وَوَصَلَ إِلَى بِلَادِ كَنْعَانَ، وَهِيَ الَّتِي فِيهَا يَعْقُوبُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَأَوْلَادُهُ. وَحِينَئِذٍ احْتَاطَ يُوسُفُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، لِلنَّاسِ فِي غَلَّاتِهِمْ، وَجَمَعَهَا أَحْسَنَ جَمْعٍ، فَحَصَلَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مَبْلَغٌ عَظِيمٌ، وأهراءَ مُتَعَدِّدَةٌ هَائِلَةٌ، وَوَرَدَ عَلَيْهِ النَّاسُ مِنْ سَائِرِ الْأَقَالِيمِ وَالْمُعَامَلَاتِ، يَمْتَارُونَ لِأَنْفُسِهِمْ وَعِيَالِهِمْ، فَكَانَ لَا يُعْطَى الرَّجُلُ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ حَمْلِ بِعِيرٍ فِي السَّنَةِ. وَكَانَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، لَا يُشْبِعُ نَفْسَهُ وَلَا يَأْكُلُ هُوَ وَالْمَلِكُ وَجُنُودُهُمَا إِلَّا أَكْلَةً وَاحِدَةً فِي وَسَطِ النَّهَارِ، حَتَّى يَتَكَفَّى النَّاسُ بِمَا فِي أَيْدِيهِمْ مُدَّةَ السَّبْعِ سِنِينَ. وَكَانَ رَحْمَةً مِنَ اللَّهِ عَلَى أَهْلِ مِصْرَ.

وَمَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُ الْمُفَسِّرِينَ مِنْ أَنَّهُ بَاعَهُمْ فِي السَّنَةِ الْأَوْلَى بِالْأَمْوَالِ، وَفِي الثَّانِيَةِ بِالْمَتَاعِ، وَفِي الثَّالِثَةِ بِكَذَا، وَفِي الرَّابِعَةِ بِكَذَا، حَتَّى بَاعَهُمْ بِأَنْفُسِهِمْ وَأَوْلَادِهِمْ بَعْدَمَا تَمَلَّك عَلَيْهِمْ جَمِيعَ مَا يَمْلِكُونَ، ثُمَّ أَعْتَقَهُمْ وَرَدَّ عَلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ كُلَّهَا، اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِصِحَّةِ ذَلِكَ، وَهُوَ مِنَ الْإِسْرَائِيلِيَّاتِ الَّتِي لَا تُصَدَّقُ وَلَا تَكْذَّبُ.

وَالْغَرَضُ أَنَّهُ كَانَ فِي جُمْلَةِ مِنْ وَرَدَ لِلْمِيرَةِ إخوةُ يُوسُفَ، عَنْ أَمْرِ أَبِيهِمْ لَهُمْ فِي ذَلِكَ، فَإِنَّهُ بَلَغَهُمْ أَنَّ عَزِيزَ مِصْرَ يُعْطِي النَّاسَ الطَّعَامَ بِثَمَنِهِ، فَأَخَذُوا مَعَهُمْ بِضَاعَةً يَعْتَاضُونَ بِهَا طَعَامًا، وَرَكِبُوا عَشَرَةُ نَفَرٍ، وَاحْتَبَسَ يَعْقُوبُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، عِنْدَهُ بِنْيَامِينَ شَقِيقَ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِمَا السَّلَامُ، وَكَانَ أَحَبَّ وَلَدِهِ إِلَيْهِ بَعْدَ يُوسُفَ. فَلَمَّا دَخَلُوا عَلَى يُوسُفَ، وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ فِي أُبَّهَتِهِ وَرِيَاسَتِهِ وَسِيَادَتِهِ، عَرَفَهُمْ حِينَ نَظَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ، ﴿وَهُمْ لَهُ مُنْكِرُونَ﴾ أَيْ: لَا يَعْرِفُونَهُ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ فَارَقُوهُ وَهُوَ صَغِيرٌ حَدَثٌ فَبَاعُوهُ لِلسَّيَّارَةِ، وَلَمْ يَدْرُوا أَيْنَ يَذْهَبُونَ بِهِ، وَلَا كَانُوا يَسْتَشْعِرُونَ فِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ أَنْ يَصِيرَ إِلَى مَا صَارَ إِلَيْهِ، فَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَعْرِفُوهُ، وأما هو فعرفهم.

فَذَكَرَ السُّدِّيُّ وَغَيْرُهُ: أَنَّهُ شَرَعَ يُخَاطِبُهُمْ، فَقَالَ لَهُمْ كَالْمُنْكِرِ عَلَيْهِمْ: مَا أَقْدَمُكُمْ بِلَادِي؟ قَالُوا: أَيُّهَا الْعَزِيزُ، إِنَّا قَدِمْنَا لِلْمِيرَةِ. قَالَ: فَلَعَلَّكُمْ عُيُونٌ؟ قَالُوا: مَعَاذَ اللَّهِ. قَالَ: فَمَنْ أَيْنَ أَنْتُمْ؟ قَالُوا: مِنْ بِلَادِ كَنْعَانَ، وَأَبُونَا يَعْقُوبُ نَبِيُّ اللَّهِ. قَالَ: وَلَهُ أَوْلَادٌ غَيْرُكُمْ؟ قَالُوا: نَعَمْ، كُنَّا اثْنَى عَشَرَ، فَذَهَبَ أَصْغَرُنَا، هَلَكَ فِي البَرِيَّة، وَكَانَ أَحَبَّنَا إِلَى أَبِيهِ، وَبَقِيَ شَقِيقُهُ فَاحْتَبَسَهُ أَبُوهُ لِيَتَسَلَّى بِهِ عَنْهُ. فَأَمْرٌ بِإِنْزَالِهِمْ وَإِكْرَامِهِمْ.

﴿وَلَمَّا جَهَّزَهُمْ بِجَهَازِهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: وَفَّاهم كَيْلَهُمْ، وَحَمَّلَ لَهُمْ أَحْمَالَهُمْ قَالَ: ائْتُونِي بِأَخِيكُمْ هَذَا الَّذِي ذَكَرْتُمْ، لِأَعْلَمَ صِدْقَكُمْ فِيمَا ذَكَرْتُمْ، ﴿أَلا تَرَوْنَ أَنِّي أُوفِي الْكَيْلَ وَأَنَا خَيْرُ الْمُنزلِينَ﴾ يُرَغِّبُهُمْ فِي الرُّجُوعِ إِلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ رَهَّبَهم فَقَالَ: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ تَأْتُونِي بِهِ فَلا كَيْلَ لَكُمْ عِنْدِي وَلا تَقْرَبُونِ﴾ أَيْ: إِنْ لَمْ تَقْدَمُوا بِهِ مَعَكُمْ فِي الْمَرَّةِ الثَّانِيَةِ، فَلَيْسَ لَكُمْ عِنْدِي مِيرَةٌ، ﴿وَلا تَقْرَبُونِ قَالُوا سَنُرَاوِدُ عَنْهُ أَبَاهُ وَإِنَّا لَفَاعِلُونَ﴾ أَيْ: سَنَحْرِصُ عَلَى مَجِيئِهِ إِلَيْكَ بِكُلِّ مُمْكِنٍ وَلَا نُبْقِي مَجْهُودًا لِتَعْلَمَ صِدْقَنَا فِيمَا قُلْنَاهُ.

وَذَكَرَ السُّدِّيُّ: أَنَّهُ أَخَذَ مِنْهُمْ رَهَائِنَ حَتَّى يَقْدُمُوا بِهِ مَعَهُمْ. وَفِي هَذَا نَظَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَحْسَنَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَرَغَّبَهُمْ كَثِيرًا، وَهَذَا لِحِرْصِهِ عَلَى رُجُوعِهِمْ.

﴿وَقَالَ لِفِتْيَانِهِ﴾ أَيْ: غِلْمَانِهِ ﴿اجْعَلُوا بِضَاعَتَهُمْ﴾ وَهِيَ الَّتِي قَدِمُوا بِهَا لِيَمْتَارُوا عِوَضًا عَنْهَا ﴿فِي رِحَالِهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: فِي أَمْتِعَتِهِمْ مِنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَشْعُرُونَ، ﴿لَعَلَّهُمْ يَرْجِعُونَ﴾ بِهَا.

قِيلَ: خَشِيَ يُوسُفُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، أَلَّا يَكُونَ عِنْدَهُمْ بِضَاعَةٌ أُخْرَى يَرْجِعُونَ لِلْمِيرَةِ بِهَا. وَقِيلَ: تَذَمَّمَ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْ أَبِيهِ وَإِخْوَتِهِ عِوَضًا عَنِ الطَّعَامِ. وَقِيلَ: أَرَادَ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُمْ إِذَا وَجَدُوهَا فِي مَتَاعِهِمْ تَحَرُّجًا وَتَوَرُّعًا لِأَنَّهُ يَعْلَمُ ذَلِكَ مِنْهُمْ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

---

## 12:63-64 — verses 63-64 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty informs us about them, that they returned to their father: {They said, "O our father, the measure has been withheld from us"}, meaning after this time, unless you send our brother Benjamin with us. So send him with us so that we may obtain the measure.

Some of them recited it as "yaktal" with the ya, meaning that he himself would obtain the measure. {And indeed we will be his guardians}, meaning: do not fear for him, for he will surely return to you. This is like what they had said to him earlier concerning Joseph: {Send him with us tomorrow, that he may enjoy himself and play, and indeed we will be his guardians}. This is why he said to them: {Should I trust you with him except as I trusted you with his brother before?}, meaning: will you do with him anything other than what you did with his brother before, when you made him disappear from me and came between me and him? {But Allah is the best guardian}, and some of them recited it as "hafizan" (guardian, in a variant grammatical form). {And He is the Most Merciful of the merciful}, meaning: He is the Most Merciful of the merciful toward me, and He will have mercy on my old age, my weakness, and my grief over my son. I hope from Allah that He will return him to me and reunite me with him, for indeed He is the Most Merciful of the merciful.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمْ إِنَّهُمْ رَجَعُوا إِلَى أَبِيهِمْ ﴿قَالُوا يَا أَبَانَا مُنِعَ مِنَّا الْكَيْلُ﴾ يَعْنُونَ بَعْدَ هَذِهِ الْمَرَّةِ، إِنْ لَمْ تُرْسِلْ مَعَنَا أَخَانَا بِنْيَامِينَ، فَأَرْسِلْهُ مَعَنَا نَكْتَلْ.

وَقَرَأَ بَعْضُهُمْ: [يَكْتَلْ] بِالْيَاءِ، أَيْ يَكْتَلُ هُوَ، ﴿وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَافِظُونَ﴾ أَيْ: لَا تَخَفْ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنَّهُ سَيَرْجِعُ إِلَيْكَ. وَهَذَا كَمَا قَالُوا لَهُ فِي يُوسُفَ: ﴿أَرْسِلْهُ مَعَنَا غَدًا يَرْتَعْ وَيَلْعَبْ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَافِظُونَ﴾ ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ لَهُمْ: ﴿هَلْ آمَنُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ إِلا كَمَا أَمِنْتُكُمْ عَلَى أَخِيهِ مِنْ قَبْلُ﴾ أَيْ: هَلْ أَنْتُمْ صَانِعُونَ بِهِ إِلَّا كَمَا صَنَعْتُمْ بِأَخِيهِ مِنْ قَبْلُ، تُغَيِّبُونَهُ عَنِّي، وَتَحُولُونَ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَهُ؟ ﴿فَاللَّهُ خَيْرٌ حفظًا﴾ وقرأ بعضهم: "حَافِظًا" ﴿وَهُوَ أَرْحَمُ الرَّاحِمِينَ﴾ أَيْ: هُوَ أَرْحَمُ الرَّاحِمِينَ بِي، وَسَيَرْحَمُ كِبَرِي وَضَعْفِي وَوَجْدِي بِوَلَدِي، وَأَرْجُو مِنَ اللَّهِ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُ عَلَيَّ، وَيَجْمَعَ شَمْلِي بِهِ، إِنَّهُ أَرْحَمُ الرَّاحِمِينَ.

---

## 12:65-66 — verses 65-66 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says: when the brothers of Yusuf opened their belongings, they found their merchandise had been returned to them. This was what Yusuf had ordered his young men to place in their saddlebags. When they found it among their things, {they said, "O our father, what do we seek?"} that is, what more could we want? {This is our merchandise, returned to us,} as Qatadah said. What do we seek beyond this? Our merchandise has been returned to us, and the measure was given to us in full.

{And we will provide for our family,} that is, if you send our brother with us, we will bring back provisions to our family, {and we will guard our brother and gain an extra camel's load,} for Yusuf (peace be upon him) used to give each man a camel's load. Mujahid said: a donkey's load, and it may be that in some languages this is called a "camel." So he said.

{That is a small measure,} this is part of the completion and improvement of the speech, meaning: this is little in comparison to what will be given in exchange for taking their brother, something that will equal it.

{He said, "I will not send him with you until you give me a solemn pledge before Allah,"} that is, that you swear by covenants and pledges, {that you will surely bring him back to me, unless you are surrounded,} that is, unless you are all overpowered and unable to secure his release.

{So when they had given him their solemn pledge,} he confirmed it upon them, and said: {Allah is Guardian over what we say.}

Ibn Ishaq said: he did this only because he found no way to avoid sending them for the provisions, which they could not do without, so he sent him with them.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: وَلَمَّا فَتَحَ إِخْوَةُ يُوسُفَ مَتَاعَهُمْ، وَجَدُوا بِضَاعَتَهُمْ رُدَّتْ إِلَيْهِمْ، وَهِيَ الَّتِي كَانَ أَمَرَ يُوسُفُ فِتْيَانَهُ بِوَضْعِهَا فِي رِحَالِهِمْ، فَلَمَّا وَجَدُوهَا فِي مَتَاعِهِمْ ﴿قَالُوا يَا أَبَانَا مَا نَبْغِي﴾ ؟ أَيْ: مَاذَا نُرِيدُ؟ ﴿هَذِهِ بِضَاعَتُنَا رُدَّتْ إِلَيْنَا﴾ كَمَا قَالَ قَتَادَةُ. مَا نَبْغِي وَرَاءَ هَذَا ؟ إِنَّ بِضَاعَتَنَا رُدَّتْ إِلَيْنَا وَقَدْ أُوفِيَ لَنَا الْكَيْلُ.

﴿وَنَمِيرُ أَهْلَنَا﴾ أَيْ: إِذَا أَرْسَلْتَ أَخَانَا مَعَنَا نَأْتِي بِالْمِيرَةِ إِلَى أَهْلِنَا، ﴿وَنَحْفَظُ أَخَانَا وَنزدَادُ كَيْلَ بَعِيرٍ﴾ وَذَلِكَ أَنَّ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، كَانَ يُعْطِي كُلَّ رَجُلٍ حِمْلَ بَعِيرٍ. وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: حِمْلَ حِمَارٍ. وَقَدْ يُسَمَّى فِي بَعْضِ اللُّغَاتِ بَعِيرًا، كَذَا قَالَ.

﴿ذَلِكَ كَيْلٌ يَسِيرٌ﴾ هَذَا مِنْ تَمَامِ الْكَلَامِ وَتَحْسِينِهِ، أَيْ: إِنَّ هَذَا يَسِيرٌ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ أَخْذِ أَخِيهِمْ مَا يَعْدِلُ هَذَا.

﴿قَالَ لَنْ أُرْسِلَهُ مَعَكُمْ حَتَّى تُؤْتُونِ مَوْثِقًا مِنَ اللَّهِ﴾ أَيْ: تَحْلِفُونَ بِالْعُهُودِ وَالْمَوَاثِيقِ، ﴿لَتَأْتُنَّنِي بِهِ إِلا أَنْ يُحَاطَ بِكُمْ﴾ إِلَّا أَنْ تُغْلَبُوا كُلُّكُمْ وَلَا تَقْدِرُونَ عَلَى تَخْلِيصِهِ.

﴿فَلَمَّا آتَوْهُ مَوْثِقَهُمْ﴾ أَكَّدَهُ عَلَيْهِمْ فَقَالَ: ﴿اللَّهُ عَلَى مَا نَقُولُ وَكِيلٌ﴾

قَالَ ابْنُ إِسْحَاقَ: وَإِنَّمَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَجِدْ بُدًّا مَنْ بَعْثِهِمْ لِأَجْلِ الْمِيرَةِ، الَّتِي لَا غنى لهم عنها، فبعثه معهم.

---

## 12:67-68 — verses 67-68 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says, reporting about Ya'qub (peace be upon him): that he instructed his sons, when he had equipped them along with their brother Benjamin to go to Egypt, not to enter all together through a single gate, but to enter through separate gates. This is because, as Ibn Abbas, Muhammad ibn Ka'b, Mujahid, al-Dahhak, Qatadah, and al-Suddi said, he feared for them the evil eye. That was because they were possessed of good looks, fine appearance, comely form, and radiance, so he feared that people might strike them with their eyes. For the evil eye is real; it can bring a horseman down from his horse.

Ibn Abi Hatim reported from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i concerning His saying, {and enter through separate gates}, that he said: he knew that he would encounter his brothers at some of the gates.

As for His saying, {and I cannot avail you anything against Allah}, meaning: this precaution does not repel the decree and judgment of Allah. For when Allah wills a thing, it cannot be opposed or prevented. {Judgment belongs to none but Allah. In Him I have placed my trust, and in Him let those who trust place their trust. And when they entered from where their father had commanded them, it did not avail them anything against Allah, except a need in the soul of Ya'qub which he satisfied}. They said: this was the warding off of the evil eye's affliction upon them. {And indeed he was possessed of knowledge because of what We had taught him}. Qatadah and al-Thawri said: meaning, one who acted upon his knowledge. Ibn Jarir said: meaning, possessed of knowledge because We had taught it to him. {But most of mankind do not know}.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى، إِخْبَارًا عَنْ يَعْقُوبَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: إِنَّهُ أَمَرَ بَنِيهِ لَمَّا جَهَّزَهُمْ مَعَ أَخِيهِمْ بِنْيَامِينَ إِلَى مِصْرَ، أَلَّا يُدْخِلُوا كُلُّهُمْ مِنْ بَابٍ وَاحِدٍ، وَلِيَدْخُلُوا مِنْ أَبْوَابٍ مُتَفَرِّقَةٍ، فَإِنَّهُ كَمَا قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُحَمَّدُ بْنُ كَعْبٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ، وَقَتَادَةُ، والسُّدِّي: إِنَّهُ خَشِيَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْعَيْنَ، وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا ذَوِي جَمَالٍ وَهَيْئَةٍ حَسَنَةٍ، وَمَنْظَرٍ وَبَهَاءٍ، فَخَشِيَ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنْ يُصِيبَهُمُ النَّاسُ بِعُيُونِهِمْ؛ فَإِنَّ الْعَيْنَ حَقٌّ، تَسْتَنْزِلُ الْفَارِسَ عَنْ فَرَسِهِ.

وَرَوَى ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ، عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخّعي فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَادْخُلُوا مِنْ أَبْوَابٍ مُتَفَرِّقَةٍ﴾ قَالَ: عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ سَيَلْقَى إِخْوَتَهُ فِي بَعْضِ الْأَبْوَابِ.

وَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَمَا أُغْنِي عَنْكُمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ﴾ أَيْ: هَذَا الِاحْتِرَازُ لَا يَرُدُّ قَدَرَ اللَّهِ وَقَضَاءَهُ ؛ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا أَرَادَ شَيْئًا لَا يُخَالَفُ وَلَا يُمَانَعُ ﴿إِنِ الْحُكْمُ إِلا لِلَّهِ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَعَلَيْهِ فَلْيَتَوَكَّلِ الْمُتَوَكِّلُونَ وَلَمَّا دَخَلُوا مِنْ حَيْثُ أَمَرَهُمْ أَبُوهُمْ مَا كَانَ يُغْنِي عَنْهُمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ إِلا حَاجَةً فِي نَفْسِ يَعْقُوبَ قَضَاهَا﴾ قَالُوا: هِيَ دَفْعُ إِصَابَةِ الْعَيْنِ لَهُمْ، ﴿وَإِنَّهُ لَذُو عِلْمٍ لِمَا عَلَّمْنَاهُ﴾ قَالَ قَتَادَةُ وَالثَّوْرِيُّ: لَذُو عَمَلٍ بِعِلْمِهِ. وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: لَذُو عِلْمٍ لِتَعْلِيمِنَا إِيَّاهُ، ﴿وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ النَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾

---

## 12:69 — verse 69

### Translation

يخبر تعالى عن إخوة يوسف لما قدموا على يوسف ومعهم أخوه شقيقه بنيامين، فأدخلهم دار كرامته ومنزل ضيافته، وأفاض عليهم الصلة والإلطاف والإحسان، واختلى بأخيه فأطلعه على شأنه، وما جرى له، وعرّفه أنه أخوه، وقال له: "لا تبتئس" أي: لا تأسف على ما صنعوا بي، وأمره بكتمان ذلك عنهم، وألا يطلعهم على ما أطلعه عليه من أنه أخوه، وتواطأ معه أنه سيحتال على أن يبقيه عنده، معززًا مكرمًا معظمًا.

---

The Most High tells of Yusuf's brothers when they came to Yusuf, having with them his full brother Benjamin. He brought them into his house of honor and his place of hospitality, and lavished upon them kindness, gentle treatment, and generosity. He then withdrew privately with his brother and informed him of his affair and what had happened to him, and made known to him that he was his brother, and said to him, {"Do not grieve,"} meaning: do not be sorrowful over what they did to me. He commanded him to conceal this from them, and not to reveal to them what he had disclosed to him, namely that he was his brother. He and his brother agreed together that he would devise a scheme to keep him with him, honored, esteemed, and held in high regard.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى عَنْ إِخْوَةِ يُوسُفَ لَمَّا قَدِمُوا عَلَى يُوسُفَ وَمَعَهُمْ أَخُوهُ شَقِيقُهُ بِنْيَامِينُ، فَأَدْخَلَهُمْ دَارَ كَرَامَتِهِ وَمَنْزِلَ ضِيَافَتِهِ، وَأَفَاضَ عَلَيْهِمُ الصِّلَةَ وَالْإِلْطَافَ وَالْإِحْسَانَ، وَاخْتَلَى بِأَخِيهِ فَأَطْلَعَهُ عَلَى شَأْنِهِ، وَمَا جَرَى لَهُ، وعَرّفه أَنَّهُ أَخُوهُ، وَقَالَ لَهُ: "لَا تَبْتَئِسْ" أَيْ: لَا تَأْسَفْ عَلَى مَا صَنَعُوا بِي، وَأَمَرَهُ بِكِتْمَانِ ذَلِكَ عَنْهُمْ، وَأَلَّا يُطْلِعَهُمْ عَلَى مَا أَطْلَعَهُ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَنَّهُ أَخُوهُ، وَتَوَاطَأَ مَعَهُ أَنَّهُ سَيَحْتَالُ عَلَى أَنْ يُبْقِيَهُ عِنْدَهُ، مُعزّزًا مكرما معظما.

## 12:70-72 — verses 70-72 (shared commentary)

### Translation

When he had provided for them and loaded their pack animals with food, he ordered some of his young men to place the "siqayah" (drinking vessel), which was a vessel of silver according to the majority opinion. It was also said to have been of gold, this being the statement of Ibn Zayd. He used to drink from it, and he used it to measure out grain for the people at that time when food was scarce. This was said by Ibn Abbas, Mujahid, Qatadah, al-Dahhak, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd.

Shu'bah reported from Abu Bishr, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas concerning {the drinking cup of the king}: he said it was of silver, and they used to drink from it, and it was like the "makkuk" (a measure of volume). Al-Abbas had had a similar one in the pre-Islamic era. He (Joseph) placed it among Benjamin's belongings without anyone being aware of it, then a caller among them called out: {"O you caravan! Indeed you are thieves!"} So they turned toward the caller and said: {"What is it you are missing?" They said, "We are missing the king's drinking cup"}, meaning the measuring vessel he used to measure with, {"and for whoever brings it there will be a camel's load,"} this being a form of ju'alah (offering a reward for a service), {"and I am guarantor of it,"} this being a form of daman (guarantee) and kafalah (surety).

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

لَمَّا جَهَّزَهُمْ وحَمَّل لَهُمْ أَبْعِرَتَهُمْ طَعَامًا، أَمَرَ بَعْضَ فِتْيَانِهِ أَنْ يَضَعَ "السِّقَايَةَ"، وَهِيَ: إِنَاءٌ مِنْ فِضَّةٍ فِي قَوْلِ الْأَكْثَرِينَ. وَقِيلَ: مِنْ ذَهَبٍ -قَالَهُ ابْنُ زَيْدٍ -كَانَ يَشْرَبُ فِيهِ، وَيَكِيلُ لِلنَّاسِ بِهِ مِنْ عزَّة الطَّعَامِ إِذْ ذَاكَ، قَالَهُ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَقَتَادَةُ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ، وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدٍ.

وَقَالَ شُعْبَةَ، عَنْ أَبِي بِشْرٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿صُوَاعَ الْمَلِكِ﴾ قَالَ: كَانَ مِنْ فِضَّةٍ يَشْرَبُونَ فِيهِ، وَكَانَ مِثْلَ الْمَكُّوكِ، وَكَانَ لِلْعَبَّاسِ مثلُه فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ، فَوَضَعَهَا فِي مَتَاعِ بِنْيَامِينَ مِنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَشْعُرُ أَحَدٌ، ثُمَّ نَادَى مُنَادٍ بَيْنَهُمْ: ﴿أَيَّتُهَا الْعِيرُ إِنَّكُمْ لَسَارِقُونَ﴾ فَالْتَفَتُوا إِلَى الْمُنَادِي وَقَالُوا: ﴿مَاذَا تَفْقِدُونَ قَالُوا نَفْقِدُ صُوَاعَ الْمَلِكِ﴾ أَيْ: صَاعَهُ الَّذِي يَكِيلُ بِهِ، ﴿وَلِمَنْ جَاءَ بِهِ حِمْلُ بَعِيرٍ﴾ وَهَذَا مِنْ بَابِ الجُعَالة، ﴿وَأَنَا بِهِ زَعِيمٌ﴾ وَهَذَا مِنْ بَابِ الضَّمَانِ وَالْكَفَالَةِ.

---

## 12:73-76 — verses 73-76 (shared commentary)

### Translation

When those young men accused them of theft, the brothers of Yusuf said to them: {By Allah, you certainly know that we did not come to cause corruption in the land, and we were not thieves}, meaning: you have verified and known, ever since you came to know us (because they had witnessed good conduct from them), that we did not come to spread corruption in the land, and we were not thieves, meaning: our natures do not permit this characteristic. The young men said to them: {Then what is his recompense} that is, the thief's, if he is among you, {if you are liars}, meaning: what would be his punishment if we found among you the one who took it? {They said, His recompense is that the one in whose bag it is found, he himself shall be his recompense. Thus do we recompense the wrongdoers.}

This was indeed the law of Ibrahim (peace be upon him): that the thief is handed over to the one from whom he stole. This is what Yusuf (peace be upon him) intended. That is why he began with their bags before the bag of his brother, that is, he searched them before his, as a form of tawriya (deliberate ambiguity to conceal his intent). {Then he brought it out of his brother's bag}, and so he took him by virtue of their own admission and commitment, binding them to what they themselves believed in. That is why Allah, the Exalted, said: {Thus did We plan for Yusuf}. This is of the beloved, intended scheming which Allah loves and is pleased with, because of the wisdom and the sought benefit contained in it.

Concerning His saying: {He could not have taken his brother under the king's law}, meaning: it was not permissible for him to take him under the ruling law of the king of Egypt. This was said by al-Dahhak and others.

Rather, Allah made it possible for him that his brothers had committed themselves to what they had committed themselves to, and he knew that this was from their own law. That is why Allah, the Exalted, praised him, saying: {We raise in degrees whom We will}, just as He, the Exalted, said: {Allah will raise those who believe among you, and those who were given knowledge, in degrees. And Allah is well acquainted with what you do} [al-Mujadilah: 11].

{And above every possessor of knowledge is one more knowing}. Al-Hasan al-Basri said: there is no knowledgeable person except that above him is one more knowledgeable, until it reaches Allah, Mighty and Majestic. Similarly, Abd al-Razzaq narrated, from Sufyan al-Thawri, from Abd al-A'la al-Tha'labi, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, who said: we were with Ibn Abbas, and he related a strange account. A man expressed amazement and said: praise be to Allah, above every possessor of knowledge is one more knowing. [Ibn Abbas said: what an evil thing you have said. Allah is the All-Knowing, and He is above every knowledgeable one.] Similarly, Simak narrated, from Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas, concerning {And above every possessor of knowledge is one more knowing}: he said: this one is more knowledgeable than that one, and that one is more knowledgeable than this one, and Allah is above every knowledgeable one. Ikrimah said the same.

Qatadah said: {And above every possessor of knowledge is one more knowing}, until knowledge reaches its end with Allah. From Him it began, and the scholars learned it, and to Him it returns. And in the reading of Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud): "and above every knowledgeable one is one more knowing."

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

لَمَّا اتَّهَمَهُمْ أُولَئِكَ الْفِتْيَانُ بِالسَّرِقَةِ، قَالَ لَهُمْ إِخْوَةُ يُوسُفَ: ﴿تَاللَّهِ لَقَدْ عَلِمْتُمْ مَا جِئْنَا لِنُفْسِدَ فِي الأرْضِ وَمَا كُنَّا سَارِقِينَ﴾ أَيْ: لَقَدْ تَحَقَّقْتُمْ وَعَلِمْتُمْ مُنْذُ عَرَفْتُمُونَا، لِأَنَّهُمْ شَاهَدُوا مِنْهُمْ سِيرَةً حَسَنَةً، أنَّا مَا جِئْنَا لِلْفَسَادِ فِي الْأَرْضِ، وَمَا كُنَّا سَارِقِينَ، أَيْ: لَيْسَتْ سَجَايَانَا تَقْتَضِي هَذِهِ الصِّفَةَ، فَقَالَ لَهُمُ الْفِتْيَانُ: ﴿فَمَا جَزَاؤُهُ﴾ أَيِ: السَّارِقُ، إِنْ كَانَ فِيكُمْ ﴿إِنْ كُنْتُمْ كَاذِبِينَ﴾ أَيْ: أَيُّ شَيْءٍ يَكُونُ عُقُوبَتَهُ إِنْ وَجَدْنَا فِيكُمْ مِنْ أَخَذَهُ ؟ ﴿قَالُوا جَزَاؤُهُ مَنْ وُجِدَ فِي رَحْلِهِ فَهُوَ جَزَاؤُهُ كَذَلِكَ نَجْزِي الظَّالِمِينَ﴾

وَهَكَذَا كَانَتْ شَرِيعَةُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ: أَنَّ السَّارِقَ يُدْفَعُ إِلَى الْمَسْرُوقِ مِنْهُ. وَهَذَا هُوَ الَّذِي أَرَادَ يُوسُفُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ؛ وَلِهَذَا بَدَأَ بِأَوْعِيَتِهِمْ قَبْلَ وِعَاءِ أَخِيهِ، أَيْ فَتَّشَهَا قَبْلَهُ، تَوْرِيَةً، ﴿ثُمَّ اسْتَخْرَجَهَا مِنْ وِعَاءِ أَخِيهِ﴾ فَأَخَذَهُ مِنْهُمْ بِحُكْمِ اعْتِرَافِهِمْ وَالْتِزَامِهِمْ وَإِلْزَامًا لَهُمْ بِمَا يَعْتَقِدُونَهُ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿كَذَلِكَ كِدْنَا لِيُوسُفَ﴾ وَهَذَا مِنَ الْكَيْدِ الْمَحْبُوبِ الْمُرَادِ الَّذِي يُحِبُّهُ اللَّهُ وَيَرْضَاهُ، لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَصْلَحَةِ الْمَطْلُوبَةِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿مَا كَانَ لِيَأْخُذَ أَخَاهُ فِي دِينِ الْمَلِكِ﴾ أَيْ: لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ أَخْذَهُ فِي حُكْمِ مَلِكِ مِصْرَ، قَالَهُ الضَّحَّاكُ وَغَيْرُهُ.

وَإِنَّمَا قَيَّضَ اللَّهُ لَهُ أَنِ الْتَزَمَ لَهُ إِخْوَتُهُ بِمَا الْتَزَمُوهُ، وَهُوَ كَانَ يَعْلَمُ ذَلِكَ مِنْ شَرِيعَتِهِمْ؛ وَلِهَذَا مَدَحَهُ تَعَالَى فَقَالَ: ﴿نَرْفَعُ دَرَجَاتٍ مَنْ نَشَاءُ﴾ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿يَرْفَعِ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنْكُمْ وَالَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْعِلْمَ دَرَجَاتٍ وَاللَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرٌ﴾ [الْمُجَادَلَةِ: ١١] .

﴿وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ قَالَ الْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ: لَيْسَ عَالِمٌ إِلَّا فَوْقَهُ عَالِمٌ، حَتَّى يَنْتَهِيَ إِلَى اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ. وَكَذَا رَوَى عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ الثَّوْرِيِّ، عَنْ عَبْدِ الْأَعْلَى الثَّعْلَبِيِّ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بن جبير قَالَ كُنَّا عِنْدَ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فَتَحَدَّثَ بِحَدِيثٍ عَجِيبٍ، فَتَعَجَّبُ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ فَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيمٌ [فَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: بِئْسَ مَا قُلْتَ، اللَّهُ الْعَلِيمُ، وَهُوَ فَوْقَ كُلِّ عَالِمٍ] وَكَذَا رَوَى سِمَاكٌ، عَنْ عِكْرِمة، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ قَالَ: يَكُونُ هَذَا أَعْلَمَ مِنْ هَذَا، وَهَذَا أَعْلَمَ مِنْ هَذَا، وَاللَّهُ فَوْقَ كُلِّ عَالِمٍ. وَهَكَذَا قَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ.

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: ﴿وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ حَتَّى يَنْتَهِيَ الْعِلْمُ إِلَى اللَّهِ، مِنْهُ بُدئ وَتَعَلَّمَتِ الْعُلَمَاءُ، وَإِلَيْهِ يَعُودُ، وَفِي قِرَاءَةِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ "وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ عَالِمٍ عَلِيمٌ".

---

## 12:77 — verse 77

### Translation

The brothers of Joseph said, when they saw the drinking vessel brought out from Benjamin's belongings: {If he steals, a brother of his stole before} excusing themselves to al-Aziz from resembling him, and mentioning that this one had done just as a brother of his had done before, meaning by that Joseph, peace be upon him.

Said ibn Jubayr reported from Qatadah that Joseph had stolen an idol belonging to his grandfather, his mother's father, and broken it.

Muhammad ibn Ishaq said, from Abdullah ibn Abi Najih, from Mujahid, who said: The first trial that befell Joseph, as it has reached me, was that his paternal aunt, the daughter of Isaac, who was the eldest child of Isaac, possessed the belt of Isaac, which they used to inherit according to seniority. Whoever among the heirs kept it in her charge had it as an uncontested possession, to do with as she wished. When Jacob's son Joseph was born, his aunt nursed and raised him, so he belonged to her and was drawn to her, and no one loved anything as she loved him. When he grew up and reached a certain number of years, Jacob's heart was set on him, so he went to her and said: "O my sister, hand Joseph over to me, for by God I cannot bear him to be absent from me for even an hour." She said: "By God, I will not give him up." Then she said: "Leave him with me for some days, that I may look upon him and find comfort in him; perhaps that will console me for his loss," or words to that effect. When Jacob left her, she went to the belt of Isaac and bound it around Joseph beneath his clothes. Then she said: "I have lost the belt of Isaac, peace be upon him; look and see who has taken it, who has come upon it." She searched, then said: "Search the members of the household." They searched them and found it with Joseph. She said: "By God, it is indeed mine to keep, to do with as I wish." Jacob came to her and she told him what had happened. He said to her: "It is for you to decide; if he has done that, then he is yours to keep, I can do nothing else." So she kept him, and Jacob was never able to take him back from her until she died. He said: This is what is referred to when the brothers of Joseph said, when what was done was done to their brother and he was seized: {If he steals, a brother of his stole before}.

As for His saying: {But Joseph kept it secret within himself} meaning the statement that follows it, which is His saying: {You are worse in position, and God knows best what you describe}, that is, what you mention. He said this within himself and did not reveal it to them. This is from the category of concealing something before mentioning it, which is frequent, as in the poet's saying:

His sons rewarded Abu al-Ghaylan for his old age and good deeds as Sinimmar was rewarded.

There are many examples of this in the Qur'an, in hadith, and in language, in its prose, its narratives, and its poetry.

Al-Awfi reported from Ibn Abbas concerning {But Joseph kept it secret within himself}: he said, he concealed within himself: {You are worse in position, and God knows best what you describe}.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

وَقَالَ إِخْوَةُ يُوسُفَ لَمَّا رَأَوُا الصُّوَاعَ قَدْ أُخْرِجَ مِنْ مَتَاعِ بِنْيَامِينَ: ﴿إِنْ يَسْرِقْ فَقَدْ سَرَقَ أَخٌ لَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ﴾ يَتَنَصَّلُونَ إِلَى الْعَزِيزِ مِنَ التَّشَبُّهِ بِهِ، وَيَذْكُرُونَ أَنَّ هَذَا فَعَلَ كَمَا فَعَل أَخٌ لَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ، يَعْنُونَ بِهِ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ.

قَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ كَانَ يُوسُفُ قَدْ سَرَقَ صَنَمًا لِجَدِّهِ، أَبِي أُمِّهِ، فَكَسَرَهُ.

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أَبِي نَجِيح، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ قَالَ: كَانَ أَوَّلُ مَا دَخَلَ عَلَى يُوسُفَ مِنَ الْبَلَاءِ، فِيمَا بَلَغَنِي، أَنَّ عَمَّتَهُ ابْنَةَ إِسْحَاقَ، وَكَانَتْ أَكْبَرَ وَلَدِ إِسْحَاقَ، وَكَانَتْ إِلَيْهَا مِنْطَقَةُ إِسْحَاقَ، وَكَانُوا يَتَوَارَثُونَهَا بِالْكِبَرِ، فَكَانَ مَنِ اخْتَبَاهَا مِمَّنْ وَلِيَهَا كَانَ لَهُ سَلَما لَا يُنَازَعُ فِيهِ، يَصْنَعُ فِيهِ مَا يَشَاءُ وَكَانَ يَعْقُوبُ حِينَ ولُد لَهُ يُوسُفُ قَدْ حَضَنَتْهُ عَمَّتُهُ، فَكَانَ مِنْهَا وَإِلَيْهَا، فَلَمْ يُحب أحدٌ شَيْئًا مِنَ الْأَشْيَاءِ حُبَّهَا إِيَّاهُ، حَتَّى إِذَا تَرَعْرَعَ وَبَلَغَ سَنَوَاتٍ وَقَعَتْ نَفْسُ يَعْقُوبَ عَلَيْهِ فَأَتَاهَا، فَقَالَ: يَا أخيَّه سَلِّمِى إِلَيَّ يُوسُفَ، فَوَاللَّهِ مَا أَقْدِرُ عَلَى أَنْ يَغِيبَ عَنِّي سَاعَةً. قَالَتْ: فَوَاللَّهِ مَا أَنَا بِتَارِكَتِهِ. ثُمَّ قَالَتْ: فَدَعْهُ عِنْدِي أَيَّامًا أَنْظُرُ إِلَيْهِ وَأَسْكُنُ عَنْهُ، لَعَلَّ ذَلِكَ يُسَلِّينِي عَنْهُ -أَوْ كَمَا قَالَتْ. فَلَمَّا خَرَجَ مِنْ عِنْدِهَا يَعْقُوبُ، عَمَدَتْ إِلَى مِنْطَقَةِ إِسْحَاقَ، فَحَزَمَتْهَا عَلَى يُوسُفَ مِنْ تَحْتِ ثِيَابِهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَتْ: فَقَدْتُ مِنْطَقَةَ إِسْحَاقَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، فَانْظُرُوا مَنْ أَخَذَهَا وَمَنْ أَصَابَهَا؟ فَالْتَمَسَتْ ثُمَّ قَالَتْ: اكْشِفُوا أَهْلَ الْبَيْتِ. فَكَشَفُوهُمْ فَوَجَدُوهَا مَعَ يُوسُفَ. فَقَالَتْ: وَاللَّهِ إِنَّهُ لِي لسَلَمٌ، أَصْنَعُ فِيهِ مَا شِئْتُ. فَأَتَاهَا يَعْقُوبُ فَأَخْبَرَتْهُ الْخَبَرَ. فَقَالَ لَهَا: أَنْتَ وَذَاكَ، إِنْ كَانَ فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ سَلَم لَكِ مَا أَسْتَطِيعُ غَيْرَ ذَلِكَ. فَأَمْسَكَتْهُ فَمَا قَدَرَ عَلَيْهِ يَعْقُوبُ حَتَّى مَاتَتْ. قَالَ: فَهُوَ الَّذِي يَقُولُ إِخْوَةُ يُوسُفَ حِينَ صُنِعَ بِأَخِيهِ مَا صَنَعَ حِينَ أَخَذَهُ: ﴿إِنْ يَسْرِقْ فَقَدْ سَرَقَ أَخٌ لَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ﴾ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَأَسَرَّهَا يُوسُفُ فِي نَفْسِهِ﴾ يَعْنِي: الْكَلِمَةَ الَّتِي بَعْدَهَا، وَهِيَ قَوْلُهُ: ﴿أَنْتُمْ شَرٌّ مَكَانًا وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا تَصِفُونَ﴾ أَيْ: تَذْكُرُونَ. قَالَ هَذَا فِي نَفْسِهِ، وَلَمْ يُبْدِهِ لَهُمْ، وَهَذَا مِنْ بَابِ الْإِضْمَارِ قَبْلَ الذَّكَرِ، وَهُوَ كَثِيرٌ، كَقَوْلِ الشَّاعِرِ: 

جَزَى بَنُوه أَبَا الْغَيْلَانِ عَنِ كبَرٍ ... وحسْن فِعْلٍ كَمَا يُجزَى سِنِمَّارُ

وَلَهُ شَوَاهِدُ كَثِيرَةٌ فِي الْقُرْآنِ وَالْحَدِيثِ وَاللُّغَةِ، فِي مَنْثُورِهَا وَأَخْبَارِهَا وَأَشْعَارِهَا.

قَالَ الْعَوْفِيُّ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿فَأَسَرَّهَا يُوسُفُ فِي نَفْسِهِ﴾ قَالَ: أَسَرَ فِي نَفْسِهِ: ﴿أَنْتُمْ شَرٌّ مَكَانًا وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا تَصِفُونَ﴾

---

## 12:78-79 — verses 78-79 (shared commentary)

### Translation

When it became necessary to take Benjamin and it was settled that he would remain with Yusuf according to their own admission, they began to soften their approach toward him and try to move him to sympathy for them. So {they said, "O 'Aziz, he has an aged father,"} meaning: he loves him with intense love and finds solace in him for the son he had lost, {so take one of us in his place,} that is, as a substitute, to remain with you instead of him, {indeed we see you as one of the doers of good,} meaning: one of those who are just and fair, who are receptive to goodness. {He said, "God forbid that we should take except him with whom we found our property,"} that is, as you yourselves have said and admitted, {indeed we would then be wrongdoers,} meaning, if we were to seize an innocent person in place of a guilty one.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

لَمَّا تَعَيَّنَ أخْذ بِنْيَامِينَ وَتَقَرَّرَ تَرْكُهُ عِنْدَ يُوسُفَ بِمُقْتَضَى اعْتِرَافِهِمْ، شَرَعُوا يَتَرَقَّقُونَ لَهُ وَيُعَطِّفُونَهُ عَلَيْهِمْ، فَ ﴿قَالُوا يَا أَيُّهَا الْعَزِيزُ إِنَّ لَهُ أَبًا شَيْخًا كَبِيرًا﴾ يَعْنُونَ: وَهُوَ يُحِبُّهُ حُبًّا شَدِيدًا وَيَتَسَلَّى بِهِ عَنْ وَلَدِهِ الَّذِي فَقَدَهُ، ﴿فَخُذْ أَحَدَنَا مَكَانَهُ﴾ أَيْ: بَدَلَهُ، يَكُونُ عِنْدَكَ عِوَضًا عَنْهُ، ﴿إِنَّا نَرَاكَ مِنَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ﴾ أَيْ: مِنَ الْعَادِلِينَ الْمُنْصِفَيْنِ الْقَابِلَيْنِ لِلْخَيْرِ. ﴿قَالَ مَعَاذَ اللَّهِ أَنْ نَأْخُذَ إِلا مَنْ وَجَدْنَا مَتَاعَنَا عِنْدَهُ﴾ أَيْ: كَمَا قُلْتُمْ وَاعْتَرَفْتُمْ، ﴿إِنَّا إِذًا لَظَالِمُونَ﴾ [أَيْ] إِنْ أَخْذَنَا بَرِيئًا بِسَقِيمٍ.

---

## 12:80-82 — verses 80-82 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty informs us about the brothers of Yusuf: when they despaired of freeing their brother Benjamin, whom they had pledged to their father to bring back and had covenanted with him about that, and this was denied to them, {they withdrew} meaning they separated themselves from the people, {conferring privately}, whispering counsel among themselves.

{The eldest among them said}, and he was Reuben, though it is also said he was Judah, the one who had suggested to them that Yusuf be thrown into the well when they had intended to kill him. He said to them: {Do you not know that your father has taken from you a solemn pledge before Allah} that you would surely bring him back to him? You have seen how this proved impossible for you, in addition to what had already happened regarding your loss of Yusuf before. {So I will not leave this land} meaning, I will not depart from this town, {until my father permits me} to return to him, being satisfied with me, {or Allah judges for me}. It is said this means by the sword, and it is also said it means that He enables me to take my brother back. {And He is the best of judges}.

Then he commanded them to inform their father of the matter exactly as it had occurred, so that it might serve as an excuse for them before him, so that they might disavow themselves and clear themselves of what had happened, through their own account of it.

Regarding His saying: {And we were not keepers of the unseen}, Ikrimah and Qatadah said: We did not know that your son had stolen.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: We did not know in the unseen that he would steal anything for himself; we had only asked what the punishment for a thief would be.

{And ask the town in which we were} it is said this refers to Egypt, as Qatadah said, though it is also said it refers to another place, {and the caravan with which we returned} meaning the one we accompanied, concerning our truthfulness, our trustworthiness, our safeguarding, and our watchfulness, {and indeed we are truthful} in what we have told you, namely that he stole and that they seized him for his theft.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى عَنْ إِخْوَةِ يُوسُفَ: أَنَّهُمْ لَمَّا يَئِسُوا مِنْ تَخْلِيصِ أَخِيهِمْ بِنْيَامِينَ، الَّذِي قَدِ الْتَزَمُوا لِأَبِيهِمْ بِرَدِّهِ إِلَيْهِ، وَعَاهَدُوهُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ، فَامْتَنَعَ عَلَيْهِمْ ذَلِكَ، ﴿خَلَصُوا﴾ أَيِ: انْفَرَدُوا عَنِ النَّاسِ ﴿نَجِيًّا﴾ يَتَنَاجَوْنَ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمْ.

﴿قَالَ كَبِيرُهُمْ﴾ وَهُوَ رُوبيل، وَقِيلَ: يَهُوذَا، وَهُوَ الَّذِي أَشَارَ عَلَيْهِمْ بِإِلْقَائِهِ فِي الْبِئْرِ عِنْدَمَا همّوا بِقَتْلِهِ، قَالَ لَهُمْ: ﴿أَلَمْ تَعْلَمُوا أَنَّ أَبَاكُمْ قَدْ أَخَذَ عَلَيْكُمْ مَوْثِقًا مِنَ اللَّهِ﴾ لتردنَّه إِلَيْهِ، فَقَدْ رَأَيْتُمْ كَيْفَ تَعَذَّرَ عَلَيْكُمْ ذَلِكَ مَعَ مَا تَقَدَّمَ لَكُمْ مِنْ إِضَاعَةِ يُوسُفَ عَنْهُ، ﴿فَلَنْ أَبْرَحَ الأرْضَ﴾ أَيْ: لَنْ أُفَارِقَ هَذِهِ الْبَلْدَةَ، ﴿حَتَّى يَأْذَنَ لِي أَبِي﴾ فِي الرُّجُوعِ إِلَيْهِ رَاضِيًا عَنِّي، ﴿أَوْ يَحْكُمَ اللَّهُ لِي﴾ قِيلَ: بِالسَّيْفِ. وَقِيلَ: بِأَنْ يُمَكِّنَنِي مِنْ أَخْذِ أَخِي، ﴿وَهُوَ خَيْرُ الْحَاكِمِينَ﴾ .

ثُمَّ أَمَرَهُمْ أَنْ يُخْبِرُوا أَبَاهُمْ بِصُورَةِ مَا وَقَعَ، حَتَّى يَكُونَ عُذْرًا لَهُمْ عِنْدَهُ وَيَتَنَصَّلُوا إِلَيْهِ، وَيَبْرَءُوا مِمَّا وَقَعَ بِقَوْلِهِمْ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا لِلْغَيْبِ حَافِظِينَ﴾ قَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ وَقَتَادَةُ: مَا [كُنَّا] نَعْلَمُ أَنَّ ابْنَكَ سَرَقَ .

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: مَا عَلِمْنَا فِي الْغَيْبِ أَنَّهُ يَسْرِقُ لَهُ شَيْئًا، إِنَّمَا سَأَلَنَا مَا جَزَاءُ السَّارِقِ؟

﴿وَاسْأَلِ الْقَرْيَةَ الَّتِي كُنَّا فِيهَا﴾ قِيلَ: الْمُرَادُ مِصْرُ. قَالَهُ قَتَادَةُ، وَقِيلَ: غَيْرُهَا، ﴿وَالْعِيرَ الَّتِي أَقْبَلْنَا فِيهَا﴾ أَيِ: الَّتِي رَافَقْنَاهَا، عَنْ صِدْقِنَا وَأَمَانَتِنَا وَحِفْظِنَا وَحِرَاسَتِنَا، ﴿وَإِنَّا لَصَادِقُونَ﴾ فِيمَا أَخْبَرْنَاكَ بِهِ، مِنْ أَنَّهُ سَرَقَ وَأَخَذُوهُ بِسَرِقَتِهِ.

---

## 12:83-86 — verses 83-86 (shared commentary)

### Translation

He said to them just as he had said to them when they came with Joseph's shirt bearing false blood: {"Rather, your souls have made a matter seem fair to you, so patience is beautiful."}

Muhammad ibn Ishaq said: When they came to Jacob and informed him of what had happened, he suspected them, and thought that this was like their earlier act against Joseph, {He said, "Rather, your souls have made a matter seem fair to you, so patience is beautiful."}

Some people said: Since this deed of theirs was built upon their earlier act, the ruling of the first was drawn over onto it, so his statement was correct: {"Rather, your souls have made a matter seem fair to you, so patience is beautiful."}

Then he hoped from Allah that He would return to him his three children: Joseph, his brother Benjamin, and Reuben, who had remained in the land of Egypt awaiting Allah's decree concerning him, either that his father would be pleased with him and command him to return, or that he would secretly take his brother. This is why he said: {"Perhaps Allah will bring them all to me. Indeed, He is the Knowing,"} meaning: the One Knowing of my condition, {"the Wise,"} in His acts, His decree, and His measure.

{"And he turned away from them and said, 'Oh, my grief over Joseph!'"} meaning: he turned away from his sons and said, recalling his old, former grief for Joseph: {"Oh, my grief over Joseph!"} The grief over the two sons renewed for him the buried grief.

Abd al-Razzaq said, al-Thawri informed us, from Sufyan al-Usfuri, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, that he said: No one was given the istirja' (the saying "to Allah we belong and to Him we return") except this nation. Do you not hear the statement of Jacob (peace be upon him): {"Oh, my grief over Joseph! And his eyes turned white from grief, for he was suppressing sorrow,"} meaning: silent, not complaining of his affair to any created being. This is what Qatadah and others said.

Al-Dahhak said: {"for he was suppressing sorrow"} means grieved and sorrowful.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] from al-Ahnaf ibn Qays, that the Prophet ﷺ said: "David (peace be upon him) said: O Lord, the Children of Israel ask You by Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, so make me a fourth for them. Allah, Exalted is He, revealed to him: O David, Abraham was cast into the fire for My sake and he was patient, and that is a trial that has not befallen you. Isaac offered up the very blood of his life for My sake and he was patient, and that is a trial that has not befallen you. And Jacob, I took from him his beloved one until his eyes turned white from grief, and he was patient, and that is a trial that has not befallen you."

This is a mursal (a report with a missing link at the Companion level) report, and it contains something objectionable, for the sound view is that Ishmael was the one intended for sacrifice. But Ali ibn Zayd ibn Jud'an has many objectionable and singular reports, and Allah knows best.

The nearest explanation for this is that al-Ahnaf ibn Qays, may Allah have mercy on him, related it from the Israelite traditions, like those of Ka'b and Wahb and similar figures, and Allah knows best. For the Israelite narrators transmit that Jacob wrote to Joseph, when he had detained his brother on account of the theft, appealing gently to him for his return, and mentioning to him that they were a household afflicted with trial: Abraham was tried with the fire, Isaac with the slaughter, and Jacob with separation from Joseph, in a long account that is not authentic, and Allah knows best. At that point his sons had compassion for him, and said to him, by way of gentleness and pity toward him: {They said, "By Allah, you will not cease remembering Joseph"} meaning: you do not stop recalling Joseph, {"until you become fatally ill"} meaning: weak in body, weak in strength, {"or become of those who perish."} They were saying: if this condition continues with you, we fear for you destruction and ruin.

{He said, "I only complain of my anguish and my grief to Allah"} meaning: he answered what they said with his statement: {"I only complain of my anguish and my grief"}

meaning: my distress and what I am in, {"to Allah"} alone, {"and I know from Allah what you do not know,"} meaning: I hope from Him every good.

And from Ibn Abbas: {"and I know from Allah what you do not know"} meaning the vision of Joseph, that it was true, and that Allah must inevitably manifest it and bring it to fulfillment. Al-Awfi said, from Ibn Abbas: {"and I know from Allah what you do not know"}: I know that Joseph's vision is true, and that I will indeed prostrate to him.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] from Anas ibn Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Jacob the Prophet ﷺ had a sworn brother, who said to him one day: What has taken away your sight and bent your back? He said: What took away my sight was weeping over Joseph, and what bent my back was grief over Benjamin. Then Gabriel (peace be upon him) came to him and said: O Jacob, Allah conveys to you His greeting of peace and says to you: Are you not ashamed to complain of Me to other than Me? Jacob said: I only complain of my anguish and my grief to Allah. Gabriel (peace be upon him) said: Allah knows best what you are complaining of."

This is a gharib (singular) hadith, and it contains something objectionable.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ لَهُمْ كَمَا قَالَ لَهُمْ حِينَ جَاءُوا عَلَى قَمِيصِ يُوسُفَ بِدَمٍ كَذِبٍ: ﴿بَلْ سَوَّلَتْ لَكُمْ أَنْفُسُكُمْ أَمْرًا فَصَبْرٌ جَمِيلٌ﴾

قَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ: لَمَّا جَاءُوا يَعْقُوبَ وَأَخْبَرُوهُ بِمَا يَجْرِي اتِّهَمَهُمْ، وَظَنَّ أَنَّهَا كَفَعْلَتِهِمْ بِيُوسُفَ ﴿قَالَ بَلْ سَوَّلَتْ لَكُمْ أَنْفُسُكُمْ أَمْرًا فَصَبْرٌ جَمِيلٌ﴾ .

وَقَالَ بَعْضُ النَّاسِ: لَمَّا كَانَ صَنِيعُهُمْ هَذَا مُرَتَّبًا عَلَى فِعْلِهِمُ الْأَوَّلِ، سُحب حُكْمُ الْأَوَّلِ عَلَيْهِ، وَصَحَّ قَوْلُهُ: ﴿بَلْ سَوَّلَتْ لَكُمْ أَنْفُسُكُمْ أَمْرًا فَصَبْرٌ جَمِيلٌ﴾

ثُمَّ تَرَجَّى مِنَ اللَّهِ أَنْ يَرُدَّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْلَادَهُ الثَّلَاثَةَ: يُوسُفَ وأخاه بنيامين، وروبيل الذي أقام بديار مِصْرَ يَنْتَظِرُ أَمْرَ اللَّهِ فِيهِ، إِمَّا أَنْ يَرْضَى عَنْهُ أَبُوهُ فَيَأْمُرُهُ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَيْهِ، وَإِمَّا أَنْ يَأْخُذَ أَخَاهُ خُفْيَةً؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿عَسَى اللَّهُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَنِي بِهِمْ جَمِيعًا إِنَّهُ هُوَ الْعَلِيمُ﴾ أَيِ: الْعَلِيمُ بِحَالِي، ﴿الْحَكِيمُ﴾ فِي أَفْعَالِهِ وَقَضَائِهِ وَقَدَرِهِ.

﴿وَتَوَلَّى عَنْهُمْ وَقَالَ يَا أَسَفَى عَلَى يُوسُفَ﴾ أَيْ: أَعْرَضَ عَنْ بَنِيهِ وَقَالَ مُتَذَكِّرًا حُزنَ يُوسُفَ الْقَدِيمَ الْأَوَّلَ: ﴿يَا أَسَفَى عَلَى يُوسُفَ﴾ جَدَّد لَهُ حزنُ الِابْنَيْنِ الْحُزْنَ الدَّفِينَ.

قَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، أَخْبَرَنَا الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ العُصْفُريّ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: لَمْ يُعْطَ أَحَدٌ غيرَ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ الِاسْتِرْجَاعَ، أَلَّا تَسْمَعُونَ إِلَى قَوْلِ يَعْقُوبَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: ﴿يَا أَسَفَى عَلَى يُوسُفَ وَابْيَضَّتْ عَيْنَاهُ مِنَ الْحُزْنِ فَهُوَ كَظِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: سَاكِتٌ لَا يَشْكُو أَمْرَهُ إِلَى مَخْلُوقٍ قَالَهُ قَتَادَةُ وَغَيْرُهُ.

وَقَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ: ﴿فَهُوَ كَظِيمٌ﴾ كَمِيدٌ حَزِينٌ.

قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا حَمَّادُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ [حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو مُوسَى] ، عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ زَيْدٍ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، عَنْ الْأَحْنَفِ بْنِ قَيْسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: "إِنَّ دَاوُدَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، قَالَ: يَا رَبِّ، إِنَّ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ يَسْأَلُونَكَ بِإِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ، فَاجْعَلْنِي لَهُمْ رَابِعًا. فَأَوْحَى اللَّهُ تَعَالَى إِلَيْهِ أَنْ يَا دَاوُدُ، إِنَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ أُلْقِيَ فِي النَّارِ بِسَبَبِي فَصَبَرَ، وَتِلْكَ بَلِيَّةٌ لَمْ تَنَلْكَ، وَإِنَّ إِسْحَاقَ بَذَلَ مُهْجَةَ دَمِهِ فِي سَبَبِي فَصَبَرَ، وَتِلْكَ بَلِيَّةٌ لَمْ تَنَلْكَ، وَإِنَّ يَعْقُوبَ أَخَذْتُ مِنْهُ حَبِيبَهُ حَتَّى ابْيَضَّتْ عَيْنَاهُ مِنَ الْحُزْنِ، فَصَبَرَ، وَتِلْكَ بَلِيَّةٌ لَمْ تَنَلْكَ".

وَهَذَا مُرْسَلٌ، وَفِيهِ نَكَارَةٌ ؛ فَإِنَّ الصَّحِيحَ أَنَّ إِسْمَاعِيلَ هُوَ الذَّبِيحُ، وَلَكِنَّ عَلِيَّ بْنَ زَيْدِ بْنِ جُدْعَان لَهُ مَنَاكِيرُ وَغَرَائِبُ كَثِيرَةٌ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَأَقْرَبُ مَا فِي هَذَا أَنْ يَكُونَ قَدْ حَكَاهُ الْأَحْنَفُ بْنُ قَيْسٍ، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، عَنْ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ كَكَعْبٍ وَوَهْبٍ وَنَحْوِهِمَا، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ، فَإِنَّ الْإِسْرَائِيلِيِّينَ يَنْقُلُونَ أَنَّ يَعْقُوبَ كَتَبَ إِلَى يُوسُفَ لَمَّا احْتَبَسَ أَخَاهُ بِسَبَبِ السَّرِقَةِ يَتَلَطَّفُ لَهُ فِي رَدِّهِ، وَيَذْكُرُ لَهُ أَنَّهُمْ أَهْلُ بَيْتٍ مُصَابُونَ بِالْبَلَاءِ، فَإِبْرَاهِيمُ ابْتُلِيَ بِالنَّارِ، وَإِسْحَاقُ بِالذَّبْحِ، وَيَعْقُوبُ بِفِرَاقِ يُوسُفَ، فِي حَدِيثٍ طَوِيلٍ لَا يَصِحُّ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ، فَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ رَقَّ لَهُ بَنُوهُ، وَقَالُوا لَهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الرِّفْقِ بِهِ وَالشَّفَقَةِ عَلَيْهِ: ﴿قَالُوا تَاللَّهِ تَفْتَأُ تَذْكُرُ يُوسُفَ﴾ أَيْ: لَا تُفَارِقُ تَذَكُّر يُوسُفَ، ﴿حَتَّى تَكُونَ حَرَضًا﴾ أَيْ: ضَعِيفَ الْجِسْمِ، ضَعِيفَ الْقُوَّةِ، ﴿أَوْ تَكُونَ مِنَ الْهَالِكِينَ﴾ يَقُولُونَ: وَإِنِ اسْتَمَرَّ بِكَ هَذَا الْحَالُ خَشِينَا عَلَيْكَ الْهَلَاكَ وَالتَّلَفَ.

﴿قَالَ إِنَّمَا أَشْكُو بَثِّي وَحُزْنِي إِلَى اللَّهِ﴾ أَيْ: أَجَابَهُمْ عَمَّا قَالُوا بِقَوْلِهِ: ﴿إِنَّمَا أَشْكُو بَثِّي وَحُزْنِي﴾

أَيْ: هَمِّي وَمَا أَنَا فِيهِ ﴿إِلَى اللَّهِ﴾ وَحَدَّهُ ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مِنَ اللَّهِ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ أَيْ: أَرْجُو مِنْهُ كُلَّ خَيْرٍ.

وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مِنَ اللَّهِ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [يَعْنِي رُؤْيَا يُوسُفَ أَنَّهَا صِدْقٌ وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يُظْهِرَهَا وَيُنْجِزَهَا. وَقَالَ الْعَوْفِيُّ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَأَعْلَمُ مِنَ اللَّهِ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ أَعْلَمُ أَنَّ رُؤْيَا يُوسُفَ صَادِقَةٌ، وَأَنِّي سَوْفَ أَسْجُدُ لَهُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا الْحَسَنُ بْنُ عَرَفَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ عَبْدِ الْمَلِكِ بْنِ أَبِي غَنَيَّة، عَنْ حَفْصِ بْنِ عُمَرَ بْنِ أَبِي الزُّبَيْرِ، عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "كَانَ لِيَعْقُوبَ النَّبِيِّ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، أَخٌ مُؤاخ لَهُ، فَقَالَ لَهُ ذَاتَ يَوْمٍ: مَا الَّذِي أَذْهَبَ بَصَرَكَ وَقَوَّسَ ظَهْرَكَ؟ قَالَ: الَّذِي أَذْهَبَ بَصَرِي الْبُكَاءُ عَلَى يُوسُفَ، وَأَمَّا الَّذِي قَوَّسَ ظَهْرِي فَالْحُزْنُ عَلَى بِنْيَامِينَ، فَأَتَاهُ جِبْرِيلُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، فَقَالَ: يَا يَعْقُوبُ، إِنَّ اللَّهَ يُقرئك السَّلَامَ وَيَقُولُ لَكَ: أَمَا تَسْتَحْيِي أَنْ تَشْكُوَنِي إِلَى غَيْرِي؟ فَقَالَ يَعْقُوبُ: إِنَّمَا أَشْكُو بَثِّي وَحُزْنِي إِلَى اللَّهِ. فَقَالَ جِبْرِيلُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا تَشْكُو" .

وَهَذَا حَدِيثٌ غَرِيبٌ، فيه نكارة.

---

## 12:87-88 — verses 87-88 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says, informing about Ya'qub (peace be upon him), that he urged his sons to go out into the land to seek news of Yusuf and his brother Benjamin.

Tahassus (seeking out news) applies to good things, while tajassus (spying) is used for evil things.

He roused them, gave them glad tidings, and commanded them not to despair of God's mercy, meaning: do not cut off your hope and expectation in God regarding what you seek and intend, for none cuts off hope and falls into despair of God except the disbelieving people.

His saying, {So when they entered before him}: the intended meaning of the sentence is: they went and entered the land of Egypt, and entered before Yusuf. {They said, "O Aziz, calamity has befallen us and our family"}, meaning from drought, famine, and scarcity of food. {And we have brought merchandise of little worth}, meaning: and with us is the price of the food which you would supply us, and it is a small price. This was said by Mujahid, al-Hasan, and more than one other.

Ibn Abbas said: it refers to poor quality goods that would not be accepted, like a worn-out sack, a rope, or something similar. In another report from him: it refers to inferior coins that would only be accepted at a discount. Qatadah and al-Suddi said likewise.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr [and Ikrimah] said: it refers to debased coins.

Abu Salih said: it is pine nuts and green seeds.

Al-Dahhak said: worthless goods that would not be accepted.

Abu Salih said: they brought green terebinth seeds and pine nuts.

The root meaning of izja (driving forth something of little worth) is pushing something along due to its weakness, as Hatim al-Ta'i said:

Let a driven-away guest weep over Milhan, and a widow who drives her orphan along together with the night.

And A'sha of Banu Tha'labah said:

The one who gives a hundred noble she-camels and their attendant, protected ones, driving their young along behind them.

His saying, informing about them: {So give us full measure}, meaning: give us, for this small price, what you used to give us before that. Ibn Mas'ud read it as: "So load our mounts and give charity to us."

Ibn Jurayj said: {and give charity to us} means by returning our brother to us.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr and al-Suddi said: {and give charity to us} means: they are saying, give us charity by accepting this merchandise of little worth, and overlook its deficiency.

Sufyan ibn Uyaynah was asked: was charity forbidden to any of the prophets before the Prophet ﷺ? He said: have you not heard His saying, {So give us full measure and give charity to us; indeed God rewards those who give charity}? This was narrated by Ibn Jarir from al-Harith, from al-Qasim, from him.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Marwan ibn Mu'awiyah told us, from Uthman ibn al-Aswad: I heard Mujahid being asked: is it disliked for a man to say in his supplication, "O God, give charity to me"? He said: yes, for charity is only for one who seeks reward.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُخْبِرًا عَنْ يَعْقُوبَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، إِنَّهُ نَدَبَ بَنِيهِ عَلَى الذَّهَابِ فِي الْأَرْضِ، يَسْتَعْلِمُونَ أَخْبَارَ يُوسُفَ وَأَخِيهِ بِنْيَامِينَ.

وَالتَّحَسُّسُ يَكُونُ فِي الْخَيْرِ، وَالتَّجَسُّسُ يُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي الشَّرِّ.

ونَهّضهم وَبَشَّرَهُمْ وَأَمْرَهُمْ أَلَّا يَيْأَسُوا مِنْ رُوحِ اللَّهِ، أَيْ: لَا يَقْطَعُوا رَجَاءَهُمْ وَأَمَلَهُمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ فِيمَا يَرُومُونَهُ وَيَقْصِدُونَهُ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَقْطَعُ الرَّجَاءَ، وَيَقْطَعُ الْإِيَاسَ مِنَ اللَّهِ إِلَّا الْقَوْمُ الْكَافِرُونَ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَلَمَّا دَخَلُوا عَلَيْهِ﴾ تَقْدِيرُ الْكَلَامِ: فَذَهَبُوا فَدَخَلُوا بلد مصر، ودخلوا على يوسف، ﴿قَالُوا يَا أَيُّهَا الْعَزِيزُ مَسَّنَا وَأَهْلَنَا الضُّرُّ﴾ يَعْنُونَ مِنَ الْجَدْبِ وَالْقَحْطِ وَقِلَّةِ الطَّعَامِ، ﴿وَجِئْنَا بِبِضَاعَةٍ مُزْجَاةٍ﴾ أَيْ: وَمَعَنَا ثَمَنُ الطَّعَامِ الَّذِي تَمْتَارُهُ، وَهُوَ ثَمَنٌ قَلِيلٌ. قَالَهُ مُجَاهِدٌ، وَالْحَسَنُ، وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: الرَّدِيءُ لَا يَنفُق، مِثْلَ خَلَق الغِرارة، وَالْحَبْلِ، وَالشَّيْءِ، وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ عَنْهُ: الدَّرَاهِمُ الرَّدِيئَةُ الَّتِي لَا تَجُوزُ إِلَّا بِنُقْصَانٍ. وَكَذَا قَالَ قَتَادَةُ، والُّسدي.

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ [وَعِكْرِمَةُ] هِيَ الدَّرَاهِمُ الفُسُول.

وَقَالَ أَبُو صَالِحٍ: هُوَ الصَّنَوْبَرُ وَحَبَّةُ الْخَضْرَاءِ.

وَقَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ: كَاسِدَةٌ لَا تُنْفَقُ.

وَقَالَ أَبُو صَالِحٍ: جَاءُوا بحَبِّ البُطْم الْأَخْضَرِ وَالصَّنَوْبَرِ.

وَأَصْلُ الْإِزْجَاءِ: الدَّفْعُ لِضَعْفِ الشَّيْءِ، كَمَا قَالَ حَاتِمٌ الطَّائِيُّ:

ليَبْك عَلى مِلْحَانَ ضَيفٌ مُدَفَّعٌ ... وَأرمَلَةٌ تُزْجي مَعَ الَّليْلِ أرمَلا 

وَقَالَ أَعْشَى بَنِي ثَعْلَبَةَ:

الوَاهبُ المائةِ الهجَان وعَبدِها ... عُوذًا تُزَجِّي خَلْفَها أطْفَالَها 

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ إِخْبَارًا عَنْهُمْ: ﴿فَأَوْفِ لَنَا الْكَيْلَ﴾ أَيْ: أَعْطِنَا بِهَذَا الثَّمَنِ الْقَلِيلِ مَا كُنْتَ تُعْطِينَا قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ. وَقَرَأَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ: "فأوقرْ رِكَابَنَا وَتَصَدَّقَ عَلَيْنَا".

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ: ﴿وَتَصَدَّقْ عَلَيْنَا﴾ برَدِّ أَخِينَا إِلَيْنَا.

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ وَالسُّدِّيُّ: ﴿وَتَصَدَّقْ عَلَيْنَا﴾ يَقُولُونَ: تَصَدَّقْ عَلَيْنَا بِقَبْضِ هَذِهِ الْبِضَاعَةِ الْمُزْجَاةِ، وَتَجَوَّزُ فِيهَا.

وَسُئِلَ سُفْيَانُ بْنُ عُيُيْنَة: هَلْ حُرِّمَتِ الصَّدَقَةُ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ قَبْلَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ؟ فَقَالَ: أَلَمْ تَسْمَعْ قَوْلَهُ: ﴿فَأَوْفِ لَنَا الْكَيْلَ وَتَصَدَّقْ عَلَيْنَا إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَجْزِي الْمُتَصَدِّقِينَ﴾ رَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ عَنِ الْحَارِثِ، عَنِ الْقَاسِمِ، عَنْهُ .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا الْحَارِثُ، حَدَّثَنَا الْقَاسِمُ، حَدَّثَنَا مَرْوَانُ بْنُ مُعَاوِيَةَ، عَنْ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ الْأَسْوَدِ: سَمِعْتُ مُجَاهِدًا وَسُئِلَ: هَلْ يُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَقُولَ الرَّجُلُ فِي دُعَائِهِ: اللَّهُمَّ تَصَدَّقْ عَلَيَّ؟ فَقَالَ: نَعَمْ، إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَةُ لمن يبتغي الثواب.

---

## 12:89-92 — verses 89-92 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Exalted says, informing about Yusuf (peace be upon him): that when his brothers mentioned to him what hardship, straitness, scarcity of food, and general famine had befallen them, and he remembered his father and the grief he was in over the loss of his two sons, along with what he himself possessed of kingship, authority, and abundance, at that point tenderness, compassion, mercy, and pity for his father and his brothers overtook him, and weeping overcame him quickly, so he made himself known to them. It is said that he lifted the crown from his forehead, on which there was a mole, and said: {"Do you know what you did to Yusuf and his brother when you were ignorant?"} meaning: how they had separated him and his brother, {"when you were ignorant"}, that is, nothing drove you to this except ignorance, given the magnitude of what you committed. As some of the predecessors said: everyone who disobeys God is ignorant, and he recited: {"Then indeed your Lord, to those who do evil out of ignorance..."} up to His saying: {"indeed your Lord, after that, is Forgiving, Merciful"} [al-Nahl: 119].

The apparent view, and God knows best, is that Yusuf (peace be upon him) made himself known to them by his own choice, with God's permission granted to him for that, just as he had concealed himself from them on the first two occasions by God's command to him in that matter, and God knows best. But when the situation grew constrained and the matter grew severe, God the Exalted relieved that constraint, just as He said: {"So indeed with hardship comes ease. Indeed with hardship comes ease"} [al-Sharh: 5-6]. At that point they said: {"Are you indeed Yusuf?"}

Ubayy ibn Ka'b read it as: "Or are you Yusuf," and Ibn Muhaysin read it as: "Indeed you are Yusuf." The well known reading is the first one, because the interrogative form indicates astonishment, meaning: they were amazed that they had been going back and forth to him for two years or more without recognizing him, while he, despite this, recognized them and concealed himself. For this reason they said in the form of a question: {"Are you indeed Yusuf?" He said, "I am Yusuf, and this is my brother." "God has indeed favored us"}, meaning by gathering them together again after the separation and after the long period, {"Indeed, whoever fears God and is patient, then indeed God does not let the reward of those who do good go to waste." They said, "By God, God has indeed preferred you above us, and we were indeed sinners."} They say this acknowledging his excellence and his being favored over them in creation and character, in abundance and kingship, in authority and also in prophethood, according to the view of those who did not consider them prophets, and they admitted to him that they had wronged him and erred against him.

{He said, "There is no blame upon you today"}, meaning: there is no reproach against you and no rebuke against you today, and I will not bring up your sin against me after today.

Then he added a supplication for them seeking forgiveness, saying: {"May God forgive you, and He is the Most Merciful of the merciful."}

Al-Suddi said: they apologized to Yusuf, and he said: {"There is no blame upon you today"}, meaning: I will not mention your sin to you.

Ibn Ishaq and al-Thawri said: {"There is no blame upon you today"}, meaning: there is no reproach against you today from me for what you did. {"May God forgive you"}, meaning: may God conceal from you what you did. {"And He is the Most Merciful of the merciful."}

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُخْبِرًا عَنْ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: أَنَّهُ لَمَّا ذَكَرَ لَهُ إِخْوَتُهُ مَا أَصَابَهُمْ مِنَ الْجَهْدِ وَالضِّيقِ وَقِلَّةِ الطَّعَامِ وَعُمُومِ الْجَدْبِ، وَتَذَكَّرَ أَبَاهُ وَمَا هُوَ فِيهِ مِنَ الْحُزْنِ لِفَقْدِ وَلَدَيْهِ، مَعَ مَا هُوَ فِيهِ مِنَ الْمُلْكِ وَالتَّصَرُّفِ وَالسَّعَةِ، فَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ أَخَذَتْهُ رِقَّةٌ وَرَأْفَةٌ وَرَحْمَةٌ وَشَفَقَةٌ عَلَى أَبِيهِ وَإِخْوَتِهِ، وَبَدَرَهُ الْبُكَاءُ، فَتَعَرَّفَ إِلَيْهِمْ، يُقَالُ إِنَّهُ رَفَعَ التَّاجَ عَنْ جَبْهَتِهِ، وَكَانَ فِيهَا شَامَةٌ، وَقَالَ: ﴿هَلْ عَلِمْتُمْ مَا فَعَلْتُمْ بِيُوسُفَ وَأَخِيهِ إِذْ أَنْتُمْ جَاهِلُونَ﴾ ؟ يَعْنِي: كَيْفَ فَرَّقُوا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُ ﴿إِذْ أَنْتُمْ جَاهِلُونَ﴾ أَيْ: إِنَّمَا حَمَلَكُمْ عَلَى هَذَا الْجَهْلُ بِمِقْدَارِ هَذَا الَّذِي ارْتَكَبْتُمُوهُ، كَمَا قَالَ بَعْضُ السَّلَفِ: كُلُّ مَنْ عَصَى اللَّهَ فَهُوَ جَاهِلٌ، وَقَرَأَ: ﴿ثُمَّ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ لِلَّذِينَ عَمِلُوا السُّوءَ بِجَهَالَةٍ﴾ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿إِنَّ رَبَّكَ مِنْ بَعْدِهَا لَغَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ [النَّحْلِ: ١١٩] .

وَالظَّاهِرُ -وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ -أَنَّ يُوسُفَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، إِنَّمَا تَعَرَّفَ إِلَيْهِمْ بِنَفْسِهِ، بِإِذْنِ اللَّهِ لَهُ فِي ذَلِكَ، كَمَا أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا أَخْفَى مِنْهُمْ نَفْسَهُ فِي الْمَرَّتَيْنِ الْأُولَيَيْنِ بِأَمْرِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لَهُ فِي ذَلِكَ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ، وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا ضَاقَ الْحَالُ وَاشْتَدَّ الْأَمْرُ، فَرَّج اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ ذَلِكَ الضِّيقِ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَإِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا﴾ [الشَّرْحِ: ٥، ٦] ، فَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ قَالُوا: ﴿أَئِنَّكَ لأنْتَ يُوسُفُ﴾ ؟

وَقَرَأَ أُبَيُّ بْنُ كَعْبٍ: "أَوَ أَنْتَ يُوسُفُ"، وَقَرَأَ ابْنُ مُحَيْصِن: "إنَّك لأنتَ يُوسُفُ". وَالْقِرَاءَةُ الْمَشْهُورَةُ هِيَ الْأُولَى؛ لِأَنَّ الِاسْتِفْهَامَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى الِاسْتِعْظَامِ، أَيْ: إِنَّهُمْ تَعجَّبوا مِنْ ذَلِكَ أَنَّهُمْ يَتَرَدَّدُونَ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ سَنَتَيْنِ وَأَكْثَرَ، وَهُمْ لَا يَعْرِفُونَهُ، وَهُوَ مَعَ هَذَا يَعْرِفُهُمْ وَيَكْتُمُ نَفْسَهُ، فَلِهَذَا قَالُوا عَلَى سَبِيلِ الِاسْتِفْهَامِ: ﴿أَئِنَّكَ لأنْتَ يُوسُفُ قَالَ أَنَا يُوسُفُ وَهَذَا أَخِي﴾ ﴿قَدْ مَنَّ اللَّهُ عَلَيْنَا﴾ أَيْ: بِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَنَا بَعْدَ التَّفْرِقَةِ وَبَعْدَ الْمُدَّةِ، ﴿إِنَّهُ مَنْ يَتَّقِ وَيَصْبِرْ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يُضِيعُ أَجْرَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ قَالُوا تَاللَّهِ لَقَدْ آثَرَكَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْنَا وَإِنْ كُنَّا لَخَاطِئِينَ﴾ يَقُولُونَ مُعْتَرِفِينَ لَهُ بِالْفَضْلِ وَالْأَثْرَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ فِي الْخَلْقِ وَالْخُلُقِ، وَالسَّعَةِ وَالْمُلْكِ، وَالتَّصَرُّفِ وَالنُّبُوَّةِ أَيْضًا -عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ لَمْ يَجْعَلْهُمْ أَنْبِيَاءَ -وَأَقَرُّوا لَهُ بِأَنَّهُمْ أَسَاءُوا إِلَيْهِ وَأَخْطَئُوا فِي حَقِّهِ.

﴿قَالَ لَا تَثْرِيبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْيَوْمَ﴾ يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْنِيبَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَلَا عَتْب عَلَيْكُمُ الْيَوْمَ، وَلَا أُعِيدُ ذَنْبَكُمْ فِي حَقِّي بَعْدَ اليوم.

ثُمَّ زَادَهُمُ الدُّعَاءَ لَهُمْ بِالْمَغْفِرَةِ فَقَالَ: ﴿يَغْفِرُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ وَهُوَ أَرْحَمُ الرَّاحِمِينَ﴾

قَالَ السُّدِّيُّ: اعْتَذَرُوا إِلَى يُوسُفَ، فَقَالَ: ﴿لَا تَثْرِيبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْيَوْمَ﴾ يَقُولُ: لَا أَذْكُرُ لَكُمْ ذَنْبَكُمْ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ إِسْحَاقَ وَالثَّوْرِيُّ: ﴿لَا تَثْرِيبَ عَلَيْكُمُ [الْيَوْمَ] ﴾ أَيْ: لَا تَأْنِيبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْيَوْمَ عِنْدِي فِيمَا صَنَعْتُمْ ﴿يَغْفِرُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ﴾ أَيْ: يَسْتُرُ اللَّهُ عَلَيْكُمْ فِيمَا فَعَلْتُمْ، ﴿وَهُوَ أَرْحَمُ الرَّاحِمِينَ﴾

---

## 12:93-95 — verses 93-95 (shared commentary)

### Translation

He says: take this shirt, {and cast it upon my father's face, he will regain his sight}, for he had gone blind from excessive weeping, {and bring me all your family} meaning all of Jacob's sons.

{And when the caravan departed} that is, it left Egypt, {their father said} meaning Jacob (peace be upon him), to those of his sons who remained with him: {Indeed I find the scent of Joseph, if you do not think me senile}, meaning: were it not that you would attribute me to fanad (senility) and old age.

Abd al-Razzaq said: [chain] Isra'il, from Abu Sinan, from Abdullah ibn Abi al-Hudhayl, who said: I heard Ibn Abbas say regarding {And when the caravan departed}: he said: when the caravan set out, a wind blew and brought to Jacob the scent of Joseph's shirt, so he said: {Indeed I find the scent of Joseph, if you do not think me senile}. He said: he found his scent from a distance of eight days' journey.

Similarly it was narrated by Sufyan al-Thawri, Shu'bah, and others, from Abu Sinan, with this same content.

Al-Hasan and Ibn Jurayj said: there were eighty farsakhs between them, and it had been eighty years since they had separated.

As for His saying, {if you do not think me senile}: Ibn Abbas, Mujahid, Ata', Qatadah, and Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: it means "you consider me foolish."

Mujahid also said, along with al-Hasan: it means "you consider me decrepit with age."

As for their saying, {Indeed you are still in your old error}: Ibn Abbas said: meaning "in your old mistake."

Qatadah said: that is, on account of his love for Joseph, which he neither forgets nor is consoled from. They spoke a harsh word to their father, one which it was not fitting for them to say to their father, nor to a prophet of God ﷺ. Al-Suddi and others said likewise.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ: اذْهَبُوا بِهَذَا الْقَمِيصِ، ﴿فَأَلْقُوهُ عَلَى وَجْهِ أَبِي يَأْتِ بَصِيرًا﴾ وَكَانَ قَدْ عَميَ مِنْ كَثْرَةِ الْبُكَاءِ، ﴿وَأْتُونِي بِأَهْلِكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ﴾ أَيْ: بِجَمِيعِ بَنِي يَعْقُوبَ.

﴿وَلَمَّا فَصَلَتِ الْعِيرُ﴾ أَيْ: خَرَجَتْ مِنْ مِصْرَ، ﴿قَالَ أَبُوهُمْ﴾ يَعْنِي: يَعْقُوبَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، لِمَنْ بَقِيَ عِنْدَهُ مِنْ بَنِيهِ: ﴿إِنِّي لأجِدُ رِيحَ يُوسُفَ لَوْلا أَنْ تُفَنِّدُونِ﴾ تَنْسِبُونِي إِلَى الفَنَد والكِبَر.

قَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ: أَنْبَأَنَا إِسْرَائِيلُ، عَنْ أَبِي سِنَان، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي الهُذَيْل قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: ﴿وَلَمَّا فَصَلَتِ الْعِيرُ﴾ قَالَ: لَمَّا خَرَجَتِ الْعِيرُ، هَاجَتْ رِيحٌ فَجَاءَتْ يَعْقُوبَ بِرِيحِ قَمِيصِ يُوسُفَ فَقَالَ: ﴿إِنِّي لأجِدُ رِيحَ يُوسُفَ لَوْلا أَنْ تُفَنِّدُونِ﴾ قَالَ: فَوَجَدَ رِيحَهُ مِنْ مَسِيرَةِ ثَمَانِيَةِ أَيَّامٍ .

وَكَذَا رَوَاهُ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، وَشُعْبَةُ، وَغَيْرُهُمَا عَنْ أَبِي سِنَان، بِهِ.

وَقَالَ الْحَسَنُ وَابْنُ جُرَيْج: كَانَ بَيْنَهُمَا ثَمَانُونَ فَرْسَخًا، وَكَانَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُ مُنْذُ افْتَرَقَا ثَمَانُونَ سَنَةً.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَوْلا أَنْ تُفَنِّدُونِ﴾ قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَعَطَاءٌ، وَقَتَادَةُ، وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْر: تُسَفّهون.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ أَيْضًا، وَالْحَسَنُ: تُهرّمون.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُمْ: ﴿إِنَّكَ لَفِي ضَلالِكَ الْقَدِيمِ﴾ قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: لَفِي خَطَئِكَ الْقَدِيمِ.

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: أَيْ مِنْ حُبِّ يُوسُفَ لَا تَنْسَاهُ وَلَا تَسَلَاهُ، قَالُوا لِوَالِدِهِمْ كَلِمَةً غَلِيظَةً، لَمْ يَكُنْ يَنْبَغِي لَهُمْ أَنْ يَقُولُوهَا لِوَالِدِهِمْ، وَلَا لِنَبِيِّ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَكَذَا قَالَ السدي، وغيره.

---

## 12:96-98 — verses 96-98 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Ibn Abbas and al-Dahhak said: {the bearer of glad tidings} means the messenger.

Mujahid and al-Suddi said: he was Yahuda (Judah) son of Jacob.

Al-Suddi said: he was the one brought forward for this because he was the one who had brought the shirt stained with false blood, so he wished to wash away that deed by means of this one. So he brought the shirt and cast it upon his father's face, and his father's sight returned.

Jacob then said to his sons at that moment: {Did I not tell you that I know from Allah what you do not know?} meaning: I knew that Allah would restore him to me, and I told you: {Indeed I find the scent of Joseph, if you would not think me weakened in mind}. At that, they said to their father, speaking gently to him: {O our father, seek forgiveness for our sins, for we were indeed sinners. He said: I will seek forgiveness for you from my Lord; He is indeed the Forgiving, the Merciful,} meaning: whoever turns to Him in repentance, He turns to him in acceptance.
